Western Rebel Army Launches Fierce Attack for Three Days: Madrid Has Not Yet Fallen; Planes and Artillery Bombard Continuously; Garrison Resists and Does Not Abandon an Inch of Land 69

Gibraltar: Although Madrid has been repeatedly attacked by the National Army in the past 24 hours, the entire city is still in the hands of the government army. It is reported that the government army is still confronting the enemy on the banks of the Manzanares River in western Madrid. The National Army initially announced that it had occupied the Segovia Bridge and the Princess Bridge on the Manzanares River. It is reported that both bridges are currently guarded by the government army and are in fierce battle with the enemy. According to a Reuters special correspondent in the National Army, the battle on the outskirts of Madrid is the fiercest since the beginning of the Spanish Civil War. The militiamen guard the solid trenches, and their courage and determination are truly admirable. Although they were attacked by the National Army Air Force and artillery fire yesterday, they were still able to stop the advance of the Moorish troops. According to a long-distance telephone message from a Reuters correspondent stationed in Madrid, the bombing and bombing in the capital this time has resulted in more than 200 deaths and injuries. Yesterday afternoon, bombs fell like rain, and shells fell around Trafalgar Square and the Cibeles Square, where the Army Department, Air Force Department, and the Bank of Spain are located. Shops in the city have been closed, and only cafes are still open. Today, a battalion of militiamen with new military equipment and a team of navy, totaling 400 people, lined up to guard the city's defense works, and the people shouted, "Long live the Republic" to welcome them. If the National Army enters the center of the capital, it is expected that there will be a fierce street battle and hand-to-hand combat. Even one alley and one house will not be easily given up. (Reuters dispatch dated 9th)

Suburbs of Madrid: According to a Reuters special correspondent in the National Army, the battle to capture Madrid, until the evening of the second day, although the National Army made significant breakthroughs in the government army's positions, it still failed to cross the Manzanares River or occupy any bridges on the river. (Reuters dispatch dated 9th)

Madrid: Today, four rebel bombers dropped twelve bombs on the city, killing at least nine people and injuring two hundred, many of whom are in critical condition. At the same time, rebel heavy artillery bombarded the city's palace and other places, causing some deaths and injuries. Currently, there are no statistics. The military committee in charge of defending the city is still urging the people not to retreat in the slightest. Today's fiercest battle was on the banks of the Manzanares River, where government troops had deep trenches and used tanks to assist in the battle. It is reported that a large number of rebel troops are still in the suburbs and are preparing to destroy the Toledo and Segovia bridges. Two bombs fell near the office of the Associated Press correspondent today, killing eight women and children who had taken refuge in a church there. (National Electric dispatch dated 8th)

Southern Suburbs of Madrid: The National Army yesterday arranged artillery positions between the Toledo Bridge and the Princess Bridge, and continuously bombarded the government army's positions. Most of the houses in the area north of the Toledo Bridge were hit and caught fire. They are still burning this morning. The government army excavated three trenches opposite the Toledo Bridge and guarded them with all their strength. Furthermore, solid defenses were built in front of the trenches, and barbed wire was laid in front of them for protection. The National Army was unable to enter for a while, so it changed its direction and attacked the northwest of Madrid. However, the government troops there also tried their best to counterattack without retreating in the slightest. Therefore, it is still questionable whether the National Army has entered Madrid. Looking at the situation in the Madrid area, the National Army has a total of four divisions, while the government army has 60,000 militiamen. Although they lack artillery, they are still guarding the northwest, south, and southeast of Madrid, and are not retreating. (Havas dispatch dated 9th)

Lisbon: The National Army officially declared today that it has not yet entered Madrid, but is holding the positions it occupied last night and is reinforcing its left wing because 20,000 militiamen had counterattacked the left wing of the National Army. It also said that because there is a strong wind and rain in Madrid, it has to postpone the attack and can only continue to fight when the weather clears. (Reuters dispatch dated 9th)

The War Becomes More Intense; Government Troops Prepare for a Counter-Offensive 70

Madrid: The Spanish government has dispatched news reports stating that Madrid, "not yet captured," is today under fierce attack from the Nationalist forces by land and air. This attack, which began at 8:00 AM, has increased in intensity with each passing hour. As this dispatch is being filed, Nationalist and government aircraft are circling overhead, and many bombs are falling on the streets. Only a few citizens ventured out to work this morning, most remaining indoors to avoid being pulverized by the bombs. From the rooftops of tall buildings, the bursting of shells can be seen in Madrid's most bustling Puerta del Sol area, as well as other places. The famous eastern boulevard, the Calle de Alcalá, has also been struck by many shells. The Nationalist forces' primary targets are, of course, the government's administrative buildings, which have suffered the greatest damage. The number of casualties in the capital is currently unknown. Yesterday, Nationalist aircraft dropped many declarations over Madrid containing a message from General Franco, the commander-in-chief, stating that his troops would enter the capital tomorrow, and that women, children, and foreign embassies and consulates would be treated with special respect. All of Madrid's shops are closed this morning, except for milk and coal shops, which are open as usual, with large numbers of women queuing outside to buy. (Reuters, 9th)

Madrid: Multiple Nationalist aircraft flew over the city at 9:00 AM today and dropped bombs, but no damage was caused. Later, at 3:30 PM, more aircraft arrived in formation. The sky was cloudy, which favored the air raid, so they bombed heavily. Simultaneously, the Nationalist artillery also unleashed its power. Land shells and aerial bombs rained down, with the central district, especially near the central market, receiving the most hits. The explosions shook the area far and wide, and countless houses were destroyed. A bomb also fell and exploded near the French Embassy. The number of casualties is currently unknown, but it is likely to exceed the 300 killed when Madrid was bombed by aircraft on the 30th of last month. The injured are being taken to hospitals by ambulances. At the same time, the government's air defenses were highly active, with anti-aircraft guns and machine guns firing thousands of rounds. Multiple government aircraft also took off and chased the enemy aircraft in the clouds, creating a dramatic aerial battle. Despite their fear, many residents forgot themselves and looked up to watch. The Nationalist aircraft, fearing being hit by machine gun fire, retreated for a time, but soon returned. The aircraft from both sides were engaged in close combat in the air, making it difficult to distinguish between government and Nationalist planes. After a period of intense fighting, neither side managed to shoot down an aircraft, so no victor was declared. (Havas, 8th)

Madrid: Twelve Nationalist aircraft bombed the city extensively yesterday. So far, it has been confirmed that over ten people have died and more than 150 have been injured, but the total number is still unknown. Most of the bombs dropped by the aircraft fell on main thoroughfares. Several bombs also struck the gardens of the former Royal Palace. One bomb hit the North Railway Station, killing one employee. Another bomb struck a monastery (which has been converted into a refugee shelter). One bomb fell near the Chilean Embassy, and another struck the Central Police Station, injuring four police officers. (Havas, 9th)

Madrid: Government troops have been engaged in fierce fighting with rebel forces in the outskirts of the city for several days, relying heavily on the militia. Our correspondent has learned of an incident on the front lines that demonstrates the militia's heroic response. When both sides were engaged in a fierce battle in Carabanchel yesterday, the rebel artillery fire was extremely intense, and the morale of the militia began to waver. Their leader, a member of the Communist Party, saw this and immediately ordered a counter-offensive. Upon hearing the order, the militia members sang "The Internationale" and advanced bravely. On the way, they encountered six rebel tanks, which fired machine guns that rained down like bullets. One militia member, disregarding his own safety, jumped forward and threw several hand grenades at the tanks, destroying four of them. By the time the other militia members followed, the young militia member had already sacrificed himself. Inspired by this, the morale of the militia was boosted, and they advanced together, eventually driving back the rebel forces. (Havas, 8th)

Madrid: A special dispatch from our correspondent embedded with the troops reports that government forces recaptured several positions near the airfield south of the city at noon today, and a counter-offensive is expected to begin soon. (Havas, 9th)

Mussolini is Willing to Make a Gentleman's Agreement with Britain; No Conflict of Interests in the Mediterranean 78

(London): A special correspondent for the Daily Mail in Rome, Mr. Playfair, interviewed Italian Prime Minister Mussolini yesterday regarding Anglo-Italian relations and Italy's relationship with Spanish Nationalist leader General Franco. The Prime Minister answered each question in detail. The questions and answers are recorded below:

(Playfair asked:) What specific measures does the Prime Minister intend to adopt to improve Anglo-Italian relations? (Mussolini replied:) "I wish for a gentleman's agreement to be established between Britain and Italy." (Asked:) Does the Prime Minister intend to divide the spheres of influence of Britain and Italy in the Mediterranean or to conclude a non-aggression pact between the two countries?

(Answered:) "Such measures would inevitably lead to new disputes. Moreover, countries have been concluding treaties one after another recently, like having the plague. I do not wish to encourage this trend. Furthermore, the interests of Britain and Italy in the Mediterranean not only do not conflict but are complementary. Therefore, neither side has any reason to be hostile to the other in the Mediterranean. The gentleman's agreement that I hope to conclude must mutually protect the interests of both parties and must therefore become a kind of mutual agreement, the nature of which must be fully understood and accepted by all other countries along the Mediterranean coast."

(Asked:) "Many people in Britain believe that the Prime Minister has already reached a secret understanding with Spanish Nationalist leader General Franco, that Italy will show sympathy during the Nationalist forces' war, and that after success, General Franco will cede the island of Mallorca in the Mediterranean (belonging to the Balearic Islands) to Italy as an Italian naval base. Is this true?"

(Answered:) "Regarding the issue of the island of Mallorca, I can clearly tell you that we have never had this in mind. And in fact, if a Nationalist leader in Spain were to consider the issue of ceding his country's territory at this time, I would not dare to respect such a leader." (Havas, 9th)

Thirteenth Anniversary of the National Socialist Party's First Uprising; Hitler Emphasizes That the National Army Will Fight for the Country When the Time Comes 79

Munich: German leader Hitler delivered a speech in Munich today on the 13th anniversary of the Munich Putsch, stating that no one except the absolutely insane could fail to believe that the National Socialist movement would last forever. Hitler was warmly welcomed by the old party members upon his arrival. The speech was delivered in the beer cellar where he had made a request to local officials thirteen years ago that was not granted. Hitler also stated that the new German army will fight and sacrifice for the motherland when the time comes, and then the world will see that within Germany, a cultural bulwark has been built to stop the rampage of the red and Jewish Bolsheviks. Interior Minister Frick has ordered the entire country to participate in today's commemoration ceremony and has advised the people not to engage in unnecessary entertainment. Ludendorff and Göring were also key figures in the uprising. After Hitler's request was rejected, he led tens of thousands of party members from the beer hall in the city center. Göring was in the second row of the procession. When they reached the Isar Bridge, a police team stopped them, raising their guns as if to shoot. Göring saw this and stepped forward, saying, "If anyone dares to shoot at us, everyone we have in custody will die a terrible death." Upon hearing this, the police did not dare to move, and the procession continued as usual until it reached the large hall in the city center, when someone opened fire on them. Hitler and others returned fire. The National Socialist Party's first uprising ended in failure. Two days later, Hitler was arrested. The following spring, Hitler was imprisoned in Landsberg. In his boredom, Hitler began to write a book to pass the time. The book "Mein Kampf," which has now been published, was written at that time. (Reuters, 8th)

Amoy Japanese Residents Strengthen Organizations; Establish Self-Denial Society and Hold Encouragement Assemblies; Strengthen Organizations and Conduct Spiritual Movements 80

Amoy Correspondence: The Japanese have recently been paying close attention to the governance and organization of Japanese residents from Taiwan residing in Amoy. For example, the Japanese consulate in Amoy has been upgraded to a general consulate. Furthermore, due to the promotion of the Japanese consulate, the Amoy Taiwan Residents Association (i.e., the Taiwan Association) established the "Self-Denial Society" organization under the premise of "following the will of the Japanese Emperor". It is scheduled to hold the "National Spiritual Revival Assembly" on the 10th of this month at the Xu Ying Academy on Minguo Road. Moreover, from the 7th to the 13th, it has been designated as "Revival Week", with the aim of encouraging residents to save on expenses and contribute to the Japanese nation. The four slogans are: (1) Do not drink or smoke, (2) Do not take the car unless there is an accident, (3) Get up early and climb the mountain, (4) Donate the saved funds to the "Service Box". In addition, the national concept of the residents is enhanced, and residents and merchants are required to hang the Japanese flag uniformly on every festival to show respect. The "Self-Denial Society" is scheduled to hold the "National Spiritual Revival Assembly" every November 10, and the 10th of each month is "Self-Denial Day". Members must pay attention to improving their lives, correcting bad habits, and not collecting membership fees, but when business requires expenses, the Residents Association will be asked to subsidize them. Multiple "Service Boxes" are set up to allow members to deposit savings into the boxes, which are opened and accounted for every month and stored in the Bank of Taiwan, so that they can be dedicated to national public cars at the appropriate time. "Service Boxes" are also set up in 13 locations in Amoy City, including the association's office and the offices of the Third and Sixth Districts. The above-mentioned Third and Sixth District offices are divided into districts in Amoy according to the autonomous organization of the Taiwan Association, just like our country's Baogjia districts. The Japanese have always had a very strict control and organization of Taiwanese people in Amoy, and the establishment of this association will further emphasize their psychological aspects. (November 8)

The Achievements of Nanjing's Emerging Industry, Quan Hua Soy Sauce Factory; New Methods of Soy Sauce Production in Large Quantities; Rich in Nutrients and Hygienic 81

Nanjing Correspondence: Soy sauce is a daily necessity for people's lives. It has always been manufactured using old methods, which not only wastes time and increases costs, but also often makes it difficult for the nutrients it contains to meet hygiene standards due to various factors. Therefore, the import of foreign soy sauce has increased sharply. The national soy sauce market is in danger of being encroached upon and is in a precarious situation. According to customs statistics, the total amount of foreign soy sauce imported in recent years, for ordinary soy sauce alone, has reached 643,141 dan, estimated at a huge value of 4,600,247 customs taels. The outflow of wealth is shocking. Industrialists with a sense of responsibility, in view of this, established the Quan Hua Soy Sauce Brewery in Nanjing last year, using new methods to manufacture and produce in large quantities to meet the needs of society. Before setting up the factory, they sent personnel abroad to investigate and learn from them. The following is a record of the general situation of the factory:

A Glimpse Inside the Factory

The factory is located outside the Hanxi Gate in the capital, at the Second Dike. The buildings are newly built and occupy a large area. All the equipment is very complete. The factory is divided into several parts, including steam, koji cultivation, koji production, fermentation, pressing, disinfection, analysis, and syrup production. All the machines are powered by steam and electricity. The steam pot for boiling beans in the steam room is as high as the roof, and its capacity is rare. The fermentation tanks are made of cement and have a total of ten tanks, each with a capacity of 80 dan of koji, and 32 small tanks, each with a capacity of 36 dan. The electric oven for baking wheat and the flour mill are unique features.

The Process of Soy Sauce

The ingredients of soy sauce are mainly soybeans, wheat, salt, and purified water. Although the soy sauce making process in this factory is all done by machine, the soy sauce time can be shortened, but the procedure is more complicated than that of the old method. For example, soybeans must be washed several times after soaking before being poured into a steam pot for steaming. The water used must also be filtered with sand before being used. The manufacturing procedure is to first mix the steamed soybeans and roasted wheat flour together with the homemade soy sauce koji, and place it in a koji-making room at a certain temperature. After 36 hours, it can be made into soy sauce koji. After the koji is made, it is transferred to the fermentation tank and the dissolved refined salt liquid is introduced into the tank to ferment for more than two months. It is taken out and pressed by machine, and the original juice is raw soy sauce. However, it must still be boiled with high heat steam and disinfected in the tank before being bottled or canned. The bottles and cans are sterilized before the oil is filled. After the sauce is filled, the container must be sterilized once more before being capped and sealed.

Production and Sales

According to Mr. Shen, a technician at the factory, since our factory started manufacturing, it has not been a year, and the results have been considerable. The average monthly shipment is 3,000 dan, with the most sales in the capital and the ports along the Yangtze River. Because the production capacity has not been expanded, there is no surplus goods to supply to Shanghai. However, the catering department of the Two-Roads Administration and the Shanghai-Hangzhou Line have already placed long-term orders.

Plans for Expansion

The factory's sales are increasing day by day, and there is a shortage of supply. We are actively expanding and plan to increase capital to several hundred thousand yuan. It is expected that if the expansion plan can be realized, the monthly production of soy sauce can reach 10,000 to 15,000 dan. We also plan to set up more management offices in various places to promote sales. The latest bottling equipment and pressing machines have been ordered from Britain and Germany.

Guangdong Province Requests Revision of the Exchange Rate Between the Legal Tender and Guangdong Silver Coins, Arguing That the Addition of 1.5 Is An Excessive Undervaluation of Guangdong Currency, Especially Unfair Compared to the Treatment of Guangxi Province 82

Guangzhou dispatch: Guangdong merchants believe that ever since the central government set the exchange rate between the silver dollar and Guangdong silver coins at an addition of 1.5, this has excessively devalued the Guangdong silver coins. In fact, commodity prices have subsequently risen, causing hardship to the lives of the people. Recently, when the central government reorganized the currency of Guangxi Province, setting the exchange rate between Guangxi currency and the silver dollar at an addition of 1.6, this aroused concerns among Guangdong merchants. Guangxi currency is usually worth only 80% or less of Guangdong silver coins. Now, suddenly, its exchange rate with the silver dollar has been set at an addition of 1.6, while the exchange rate between Guangdong silver coins and the silver dollar remains at an addition of 1.5. This clearly raises the value of Guangxi currency and devalues Guangdong silver coins, causing great losses to Guangdong merchants. Therefore, at the proposal of the Salted Fish Guild and other associations, a meeting of merchants from various trades was convened at the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce on Yangan Street on the 2nd of this month to discuss remedial measures. More than 60 representatives from over 30 trades, including the Grain Industry, Public Bus Industry, Peanut and Sesame Industry, and Salted Fish Industry, attended. Zou Dianbang was elected as chairman, and he announced the reasons for the meeting. The issue of the exchange rate between the silver dollar and Guangdong silver coins was then discussed. It was immediately decided to request that the central government accept the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce's previous proposal to revise the exchange rate between the silver dollar and Guangdong silver coins to an addition of 1.228 or 1.3. A circular telegram was immediately drafted to appeal to all parties, and representatives were sent to petition the authorities. However, the Finance Department has not provided a concrete response because the addition of 1.5 was set by the Ministry of Finance, and this case should be resolved by the Ministry of Finance. The reasons given in the Chamber of Commerce's circular telegram are excerpted below (the above is omitted): Guangdong Province has always used silver coins as its standard. Since the implementation of the policy of accepting silver, the people can no longer use silver coins as before, and there is a ban on private possession. The central government calculated that the amount of silver coins issued by Guangdong Province was insufficient to offset the silver reserve fund and used this as the standard for determining the exchange rate. The people of Guangdong Province firmly believe that this determination is unfair. To be sure, the people of Guangdong Province have no right to interfere with the over-issuance of paper money, nor have they ever heard the central government publicly deny or disapprove of its measures, nor has it denied the existence of the former government of Guangdong. The former government of Guangdong was also a government under the rule of the central government. If the central government cannot correct its over-issuance, how can it impose this loss on the people of Guangdong Province? This is the first point that should be clarified. Also, the provincial bank has a reserve fund of 100 million yuan. Based on this comparison, the difference in funds is extremely large. However, this reserve fund is the amount of silver stored, as well as the public factories and various construction projects in Guangdong Province, which have all been overdrawn by the provincial bank. The value of these industrial reserve funds is far more than 100 million yuan. Former bank president Shen has reported that this serves as collateral for the province government's overdraft of over 90 million yuan, which can be included in the calculation of the fund. Therefore, the amount of banknotes issued by the provincial bank actually exceeds the amount of funds. Moreover, the value of real estate deposited by the provincial and municipal banks has not yet been included. This is the second point that should be clarified. The central government's handling of the exchange rate system of each province should be fair. It is not appropriate to give special considerations to one province and treat another differently. The value of Guangxi silver coins has always been less than 80% of Guangdong silver coins because the silver content of Guangxi silver is lower than that of Guangdong silver. Since Guangxi Province took over the management of silver and switched to using banknotes, its value is the same as when silver coins were used. If the exchange rate between the national currency and Guangxi currency is an addition of 1.6, then the Guangdong currency should be set at an addition of 1.28 when converting to national currency, so as to avoid unfairness. This is the third point that should be clarified. In view of the above three points, we request again that the exchange rate for converting Guangdong currency to national currency be reduced, using the relative value of Guangdong and Guangxi silver coins as the comparison standard (i.e., calculated as an addition of 1.28). Guangdong has such cash and the assessed value of the above-mentioned industries. Whether Guangxi has comparable reserves is unknown, and if this causes disappointment among the people of Guangdong, there is a deep concern that the administration is unfair," etc. (November 6)

Zhejiang Fisheries Experiment Station Commences Marine Survey Work and Tests Coastal Fishing Grounds 83

Dinghai dispatch: The Zhejiang Fisheries Experiment Station previously submitted a request to build a small motor research and experimental vessel, and has been in contact with shipyards in Shanghai for construction. However, the construction costs have not yet been secured, and the project will take some time. Therefore, a merchant ship was chartered some time ago, slightly modified, and used as a temporary measure. It was test-sailed at the end of last month, carrying all the students of the fishery instructor training class attached to the station, led by teachers Xu Shangqing and others, to practice in Shenjiamen, Huludao, Putuo and other places. It is understood that the station considers marine surveys to be an essential task for promoting the fishing industry. In addition to sending staff to be stationed in Shengshan, Qingbin, Dachenshan, Nanji and other islands to periodically measure tides, water temperature, specific gravity and plankton, and record other marine conditions, it also plans to divide the coast into several areas, and during the fishing season, go to the fishing grounds to conduct on-site surveys of the number of fishing boats, fishing gear, catches, the extent of the fishing grounds, and the route of movement, etc., hoping to obtain detailed information and draw detailed illustrations as a compass for those engaged in the fishing industry. It has now appointed two technicians, Lin Shuyan and Wu Zhongyuan, together with technician Lin Maochun and technical assistant Huo Yibai, to drive the station's research and experimental vessel "Liping" and set off to various islands yesterday to begin work.

Suzhou: Planning for the Connection of Various Highways 87

These four roads are all main rural roads, and their width is based on the passage of rickshaws. The Huangli Road connects to the Suchang Road, the Muxu and Muxing Roads connect to the Sumu Road, and the Zhou Deng Road connects to the Sujia Road. It has now been decided that the earthwork for the four roads will be done by the villagers along the routes, and the roadbeds will be built by the Construction Bureau. It also plans to extend the Muxing Road to Dongting Mountain.

Wuxi: Expansion of Xicheng Electricity 90

The electricity for the urban area of this county was previously supplied by the Yaoming Electricity Company outside Guangfu. However, it was a commercial enterprise, and was later nationalized by the Qishuyan Electricity Plant of the National Government's Construction Committee. The business developed and expanded to the entire Wujin County. Yuqi and Qianzhou, etc. in the north of this county had poles erected long ago. Zhangjingqiao and Bashiqiao, etc. in the northeast, also had wires strung up and electricity supplied last month, with a total of more than 200 households subscribing. Furthermore, the Kaiyuan Township Electricity Company in this county previously purchased 150 kilowatts of electricity from the Qi plant. Recently, due to the expansion of its business, the supply was insufficient, and it sent a letter to the plant requesting an additional 50 kilowatts. Equipment is currently being replaced and the increased supply should be available soon.

Jiangyin: Earthen Cloth Bound for Shanghai Detained 91

The Shanghai Consolidated Tax Bureau's Inspection Office stated that when earthen cloth from Jiangyin was transported to Shanghai, the Jiangyin Inspection Office did not stamp the transportation permit with a "Checked" stamp, nor did it add an inspection stamp, resulting in repeated detentions by the No. 3 patrol boat. The Earthen Cloth Guild stated that this was hindering sales and sent a letter to the Shanghai Consolidated Tax Bureau requesting that in the future, when Jiangyin earthen cloth is reported for inspection upon import, if the goods match the permit, they should be inspected and released according to regulations. After receiving the letter, the Consolidated Tax Bureau stated that at around 4 p.m. on September 18, the No. 3 patrol boat found a rickshaw puller of unknown name at the Datong Company, holding several factory cloth permits from Jiangyin for pure numbers, applying for registration and stamping. It was claimed that the original goods had already been transshipped, but since there was a permit without goods, registration and stamping could not be done. The rickshaw puller was instructed to report for inspection and stamping first before transshipping in the future. A reply has been sent to the Earthen Cloth Guild that in the future, when transporting cloth from Shanghai, the goods and permits must be reported for inspection at the same time to comply with the regulations.

Yangzhou: Increasing Winter Defense Strength 92

The Guazhou Township Maritime Provincial Public Security Fourth District Department of the Second District of Jiangdu stated that the defense areas of its various teams are all close to the provincial capital. Maritime security on inland waterways during the winter defense period is particularly important. The Civil Affairs Department has allocated 1,000 new-style guns and punts to the district for cooperative defense. On the 7th, a distribution plan was decided, with two-thirds allocated to the various new waterways subordinate to the Yangtze River, to cooperate with the shallow-water gunboats in patrolling and suppressing bandits, and one-third allocated to the various inland river sub-teams to assist in flood prevention and patrolling. It is heard that each punt has eight shooters. From now on, the strength of both river and inland waterway defenses in the district will be increased, which is a blessing for the area.

Prisoners Petition for Amnesty 93

Three hundred and ten prisoners in the Jiangdu County Prison submitted a joint petition to the central government on the 7th, stating in general terms that the Republic of China had experienced successive disasters, and the nation's lifeline was hanging by a thread. Fortunately, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and the officials of the government, with their spirit of peace and struggle, were finally able to unify the country and immediately convened the National Assembly to promulgate the constitution. It is also the time of Chairman Chiang's assumption of the premiership, a moment of national celebration. It is believed that times of national celebration must be marked by special acts of grace, and laws must be amended to pardon past offenses. The prisoners have violated criminal laws due to momentary lapses, or due to the constraints of life, or because they were sentenced before the new criminal law came into effect, or because they did not understand the law. They are by no means without extenuating circumstances, and they cannot but regret and repent. Moreover, during this national crisis, it is time for men to serve the country and brave men to die for it. They regret that they have no way to volunteer for service. Therefore, they jointly implore the government to consider their patriotic sincerity, which is the vitality of the nation, and to issue a general amnesty before the convening of the National Assembly to mark the celebration, so that hundreds of thousands of prisoners can share in the special grace, return to the path of self-renewal, take up arms to defend the enemy, and fulfill their desire to serve the country.

Gaoyou: Canal Dike to Be Repaired 94

Yigou Township in the First District, fifteen li east of this county's city, has the Yunyan River running east-west through it, serving as a thoroughfare for urban-rural transportation. The banks on both sides of the township have not been repaired for many years and have collapsed badly. Once a flood occurs, the danger is extremely great. People in the town believe that the repair of the dike is urgent to prevent problems before they arise. Recently, the township office initiated preparations for repairs to strengthen the dike.

Haizhou: Rain Falls in Various Counties Under Haizhou 95

The counties under Haizhou have been experiencing drought for the past month. It has not rained for a long time, and the ditches and canals are drying up, and cracks have appeared in the ground. To date, winter wheat and barley cannot be sown, and farmers are generally worried. Until the 6th, the weather suddenly changed, and dark clouds gathered. A light rain soon fell, and it only stopped and cleared up at 4 p.m.

Liuhe: Plentiful Rainfall Celebrated 96

Since autumn, there have been two months of drought in this port, with no rain falling. The farmlands in the countryside are urgently awaiting rainfall. Fortunately, at 8 a.m. on the 6th, the weather changed, and dark clouds filled the sky. Before long, heavy rain poured down, lasting for several hours before stopping. It is estimated that there were about four inches of rain. Farmers can sow winter wheat and barley, and there is no risk of crop failure next year. The people of the entire county are all celebrating with raised hands.

Shaoxing: Construction of Roads in Urban and Rural Areas 97

The reconstruction of the asphalt road from Beihai Bridge to Dajiang Bridge in Shaoxing City has been underway, and the construction of sewers and water pipes has been completed. Work on the curbing stones and stone setting is currently being expedited. There are many difficulties in the construction costs, as they are based on housing donations. A meeting was convened on the afternoon of the 7th to decide on a method of apportioned collection, stipulating that 10 yuan be collected from each room in the first courtyard, 4 yuan in the second courtyard, and 2 yuan in the third courtyard. Regarding the Keqiao to Keyan highway, the county government had previously sent personnel to complete the surveying. The acquisition of private land, culverts, water pipes, and bridges has been designed and will begin on the 10th, using winter labor for construction.

Taizhou: Fire Destroys Entire Village 98

Yanshan, in the third district of Yuhuan County, a neighboring county of Wenling, has a total of only 20 households, all of whom are farmers. Since summer, there has been no rain, and everything is dry. Inadvertently, at midnight on the 31st of last month, a fire broke out suddenly. Black smoke billowed into the sky, and flames shot in all directions. Although they wanted to save the village, there was no water to pour on it, and they could not extinguish it, allowing it to burn for four or five hours before it died out on its own. As a result, all the residential houses of more than 20 households in the village were burned down. The disaster victims were crying loudly, a terrible sight to see.

Bengbu: Provincial Bank Organizes Agricultural Products 99

The rivers and lakes are crisscrossed in northern Anhui, and there are many lakes. Farmland relies on irrigation, and agricultural production is abundant. However, in recent years, droughts and floods have occurred frequently, and disasters have followed one after another. The rural economy is in decline, and there is no way to revive the countryside. This spring, the Anhui Provincial Government allocated tens of thousands of yuan to the Anhui Local Bank to experiment with providing loans secured by farmland in the Shouxian area to help farmers, which has been very effective. In order to promote widespread reconstruction, the Provincial Construction Department has ordered the Local Bank to establish bank offices in Fengyang, Huaiyuan, Huoqiu, Fengtai, Yingshang, Guoyang, Zaoyang, and Chuxian to specifically handle loans to farmers in various counties, and to invest in water conservancy projects, dredging rivers and ponds, to regulate finance and increase agricultural production for farmers. The Local Bank, upon receiving the order, is actively planning to implement it as soon as possible.

Local News

Expanded Anti-Drug Propaganda Campaign Begins in This City Today; People Who Use Drugs Should Quit Immediately; Anyone Caught Starting Next Year Will Be Executed 100

The Shanghai-Songhu Garrison Command, the Public Security Bureau, and other anti-narcotics agencies in this city have set the central government's two-year deadline for drug prohibition. After this deadline, from January 1, 1937, all drug offenders, according to the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Drug Crimes, will be subject to the death penalty, in addition to those who manufacture, transport, or sell drugs. This includes those who ingest drugs and administer morphine injections. At that time, all drug rehabilitation institutions will stop accepting new addicts, and those arrested will also be subject to the death penalty. The deadline is less than two months away. To seriously warn the people of this city who use drugs to quit as soon as possible in order to save their lives, a meeting was convened and it was decided to hold an expanded anti-drug propaganda campaign from today to the 20th to persuade drug addicts to quit voluntarily within this year to avoid severe punishment. The Public Security Bureau has, in conjunction with the Anti-Opium Committee, printed tens of thousands of propaganda materials, slogans, and pictures for distribution. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau has ordered all its subordinate sub-bureaus and teams to organize propaganda teams and set off to officially promote and persuade people. The Garrison Command has also posted notices to inform the public. The notice of the Garrison Command is recorded below:

Notice of the Garrison Command and the Ministry of Justice

It has been long stipulated by the central government that drug prohibition will last two years and opium smoking prohibition will last six years, and that they will be implemented on schedule. The end of 1936 will be the deadline for drug prohibition. From January 1, 1937, in addition to those who manufacture, transport, or sell drugs, who will still be subject to the death penalty, anyone who ingests red pills, Gaogen, heroin, or other compounds, or various colored pills compounded from them, or administers morphine injections for the first time will also be subject to the death penalty in accordance with the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Drug Crimes. Now the deadline is approaching and will arrive in a blink of an eye. People from all walks of life should understand the government's determination to prohibit drugs and be aware that the implementation of the ban is not far away. Those who use drugs or administer morphine injections should promptly reflect and quit the habit voluntarily before the end of 1936. If they persist in their errors and delay, the law is strict and they will not be spared. Once they are caught, this Command will severely punish them in accordance with the law, without any leniency. This notice is hereby issued to inform the public.

Pay Attention to the Lower Classes

The Municipal Public Security Bureau has decided to order all sub-bureaus, police stations, and outposts to organize propaganda teams from today to go to factories and ordinary people's homes to distribute propaganda materials, and to give oral propaganda along the way to the general coolies and vagrants. In addition, the Public Security Bureau will print various texts and illustrated posters for posting everywhere to arouse the attention of the general lower classes to the prohibition of opium and to make them understand the pros and cons of being punished by military law if they do not quit opium. In addition, various agencies will prepare various anti-drug films and lantern slides, and consult with the city's cinemas to screen them free of charge for people to visit, and will hold entertainment programs for the general public to visit and promote anti-drug propaganda. Dai Lizhen, chief of the Fourth Section of the Bureau, told a reporter from the Central News Agency that this propaganda campaign will focus on the lower classes because past propaganda campaigns have been effective for the middle and upper classes of citizens, but the lower classes have not paid attention to the textual propaganda and have found it difficult to understand. Therefore, this propaganda campaign will reach into the lower classes. There are many opium smokers among the lower classes in this city, so special attention will be paid to them this time.

Bogomolov Returns Home 103

Soviet Ambassador to China Bogomolov, who arrived in Shanghai the morning before yesterday, is scheduled to leave Shanghai for home this afternoon with his wife and the embassy's Chinese counselor, Oshanin, on the Russian ship Northern, managed by the Hongyun Company, and travel to Moscow via Vladivostok. The matter is extremely important, and since the ambassador is a member of the Central Executive Committee, he must attend, so he has requested leave to return home. He has no other mission, and the planned round trip will take a month, with the meeting lasting two weeks. He will return to China in about two months. When asked about the negotiations on the Sino-Russian trade treaty, Saratov only said that they were in progress and did not want to disclose more.

Liu Zhongying Suggests Collecting Vacant House Donations 106

Public Concession Liu Zhongying, a member of the Chinese Ratepayers Association, believes that collecting vacant house donations can reduce rents and prosper the market. Since the French Concession has already implemented it, he specifically suggested to the Ratepayers Association to ask the Public Works Department to follow suit to maintain the market. The original letter from Committee Member Liu is recorded below: Respectfully, regarding the case of the association's suggestion to the Public Works Department to collect vacant house donations, it was passed and executed at the first delegates' meeting of this year. To this day, it has not been implemented. Reading the newspaper, I learned that the French Concession's Municipal Council also believes that the number of vacant houses in the concession is increasing, which affects tax revenue. The Director-General of the Bureau suggested that if there is theft or fire in rented houses with equipment that are not rented, the owners must still ask the police for assistance, and they cannot be exempted from donations. The Board of Directors has resolved that all vacant residential houses will be charged 50% less than ordinary houses, and rented apartments will be charged 75% less. It is also stipulated that this housing tax should be based on the rent paid by the best tenant. I believe that the area of our Public Concession is several times larger than that of the French Concession, and the number of vacant houses in the concession is also greater than that of the French Concession. At this time when the Public Works Department's tax revenue is declining, it seems necessary to increase the collection of vacant house donations. The owners' payment of vacant house donations is their due responsibility. Moreover, by collecting vacant house donations, owners, seeing the increased burden, will inevitably reduce rents and rent out the houses in order to reduce the burden. At a time when everyone believes that rents are expensive and it is difficult to make a living, once rents are reduced, people will rent houses and do business. Therefore, collecting vacant house donations will not only increase tax revenue for the Public Works Department, but also prosper the market. In reality, it is beneficial to the owners and harmless. The above-mentioned measures proposed by the French Concession's Municipal Council are very fair. Our Public Concession authorities should follow suit. Moreover, this case has been resolved and passed by the delegates' meeting. Therefore, I respectfully request that you forward this to the Chinese directors and ask them to suggest that the Public Works Department implement it. This is what I hope for. Addressed to the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession.

Seven Japanese Cotton Mills All Workers United Strike Workers Present Five Conditions for General Wage Increase Japanese Cotton Mill Association Met Last Night to Discuss Solution 111

Dagongshe reported that more than 15,000 male and female workers from Shanghai, Tongxing, Donghua, and other Japanese cotton mills in Yangshupu, Shanghai, launched a joint strike to demand five conditions, including a 20% general wage increase. The Japanese Cotton Mill Association convened a meeting of managers from various mills at 4:00 p.m. yesterday to discuss solutions. Labor unrest is also brewing in factories such as Neiwaimian in West Shanghai. The details are recorded below.

Five Conditions Workers from Japanese cotton mills such as Neiwaimian, Toyota, Gongda, Xihe, Shanghai, Dakang, Tongxing, Yufeng, Rihua, and Donghua in Shanghai East, Shanghai West, and Pu East issued a joint declaration and put forward five conditions as follows: (1) A wage increase of 20%; (2) One hour of rest after meals; (3) No dismissal of any worker; (4) No torture of any worker; (5) Opposition to working extra hours on Sundays.

Joint Strike After the workers from each factory put forward the five conditions, all the male and female workers from seven Japanese cotton mills, including Shanghai Factories No. 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5, Tongxing Factory No. 2, and Donghua at 1687 Huade Road, Yangshupu, Shanghai East, launched a strike at 11:30 p.m. on the 8th. All the male and female workers were scattered on the roads near the factory during the day to inquire about news, and they still returned to their workshops at night. The order was quite good. According to the results of the investigation, there are more than 11,500 striking workers in Shanghai Factories No. 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5, 1,670 in Tongxing, and 20 in Donghua, totaling more than 15,000 people.

Negotiations Ineffective Japanese Shanghai Cotton Mill, etc., notified the foremen to enter the factory for consultation with the factory at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. The chief foreman, Litian, personally reported to the workers and admitted to increasing wages by 5%, but the workers believed that the difference between the proposed 20% general wage increase was too great and could not represent all the workers. The negotiations were ineffective. The factory then posted a notice at around 11:00 a.m. stating, "For the sake of notification, the factory has approved a general wage increase of 5% for the workers' request for a wage increase. We hope that all workers will resume work immediately, otherwise they will be expelled from the factory." At about 8:00 p.m., a reporter from Dagongshe learned the latest news that the workers had changed the first condition of a 20% general wage increase to 10%. In addition to one hour of rest after meals for the second item, it must be stipulated that there will be a half-hour rest from 9:00 a.m. to 9:15 a.m. and from 3:00 p.m. to 3:15 p.m. every day. For the fifth item, if there are extra working hours on Sundays, two days of bonus work must be given each month.

Association Discusses Chuanjin, chairman of the Shanghai Japanese Cotton Mill Association, visited Heitian, manager of Shanghai Cotton Mill, Shitian, manager of Donghua Cotton Mill, and Tachikawa, manager of Tongxing Cotton Mill (because Tachikawa returned to Japan, he was replaced by Daishi, director of the personnel department) at 10:00 a.m. yesterday to investigate the workers' strike and the conditions proposed by the workers. He then left. At 4:00 p.m., he convened a joint meeting of the heads of Japanese cotton mills such as Shanghai at the Japanese Club on Penglu Road to discuss solutions. After discussion, because the wage issue is related to all Japanese cotton mills, it is necessary to convene cotton mills that have not gone on strike to discuss together before a solution can be found. Tongxing Cotton Mill telegraphed Tachikawa, the manager who had returned to Japan, to ask for instructions.

Each Factory on Alert After the strike of cotton mills such as Shanghai Tongxing Donghua, the Yulin Road Police Station and the Grant Road Police Station in the Public Concession sent a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to suppress the strike. Japanese Marines were stationed in various factories under strict alert, and police cars patrolled back and forth. The Gongda Dakang and other cotton mills adjacent to Shanghai and other factories were deeply afraid of labor unrest, so the alert was very strict.

Each Factory Brewing Workers from cotton mills such as Neiwaimian, Toyota, Xihe, Tongxing Factory No. 1 in West Shanghai, Rihua in Pudong, Shanghai East, Dakang, Gongda, and Yufeng joined with the workers from Shanghai Tongxing Factory No. 2 and Donghua in Shanghai East to issue a declaration and put forward conditions. They originally planned to take the same steps to proceed. After the factory learned the news in advance, they were closely monitored, so it was not realized. The workers in each factory are still secretly active and brewing. If the labor unrest in Shanghai, Tongxing, Donghua, and other factories is not resolved soon, they will inevitably come to help. When the workers of the Japanese cotton mills were on strike, the British-owned Ewo Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road posted a notice at the factory gate at 10:00 a.m. yesterday to recruit new workers. More than 200 male and female workers from Japanese factories have applied.

Yarn Prices Soar After the news of the joint strike of workers in Japanese cotton mills spread to the market, yarn prices suddenly rose sharply. The opening and closing prices of yarn for the near and distant future yesterday are as follows: November opening 232.5 yuan, closing 231 yuan, December opening 223.1 yuan, closing 223.2 yuan, January 26th year 218.7 yuan, closing 218.3 yuan, February opening 216.4 yuan, closing 217 yuan, March opening 216.4 yuan, closing 217 yuan. If the labor unrest is prolonged and the current yarn is scarce, yarn prices will inevitably continue to rise.

Merchant Ship Accident 112

The Chunhe, a vessel rented by the Dalu Industrial Company from the Tonghe Shipping Company, has a load of 1,765 tons and a draft of 17 feet 4 inches. The vessel was transporting salt in Haizhou and, within the past week, ran aground at Chenjiagang Port due to receding water after being heavily loaded. After just managing to free it, another telegram was received yesterday from its shipowner, stating that on the night of the 7th of this month, when sailing out of Chenjiagang, it encountered severe gales and rainstorms with very large waves, making navigation difficult. The ship dropped anchor to avoid damage. However, the wind and waves were too strong, causing the port anchor chain to break, and one iron anchor was lost at sea. Sixty-six feet of anchor chain were also broken and lost at sea, causing significant damage. Fortunately, the hull remains safe.

Huachang Runs Aground for the Second Time

The Huachang vessel of the Yicheng Shipping Company is now determined to be carrying coal to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. The vessel has a draft of 19 feet 4 inches. Therefore, it ran aground near Wuhu last week. After being rescued and continuing upstream, the water level of the Yangtze River has been very shallow recently, and the recession is particularly fast, causing the Huachang vessel to run aground for the second time when it reached the river surface of Huangshigang. It is now unloading cargo for salvage. According to someone from the company yesterday, it is hoped that the unloading and salvage can be completed today. It was also reported that the Tongli vessel of the Tongcheng Company lost a port anchor on the Wuhu river surface, according to a telegram from the shipowner yesterday. Details were not given and a telegram has been sent to inquire.

Japanese Tugboat Collides with Yushun

The Taipingmaru vessel of the Dalian Steamship Company, towing tugboat No. 145, entered Tianjin Port. While heading towards the China Merchants Bureau wharf, the Yushun vessel of the China Merchants Bureau turned around and sailed out. Yushun honked its horn to order it to slow down, but the vessel failed to stop in time, causing the tugboat to collide with the No. 4 cargo hold door of Yushun, causing damage. Fortunately, Chief Engineers Cao and Zhu were in Tianjin and immediately went to inspect and negotiate with the Japanese vessel. The Japanese merchants acknowledged full responsibility for compensation and repair.

Zhejiang Provincial Government Approved Rice Transport to Shanghai, Jiangsu Province Did Not Obstruct, Grain in this City Not Panic 118

Since Zhejiang and Anhui provinces banned the export of rice, and Jiangsu Province promulgated measures to prohibit the export of grain, grain merchants in this city were deeply afraid that the people's livelihood in this city would panic as a result. After appealing to all parties, it is understood that the Zhejiang Provincial Government has now approved the transport of rice to Shanghai. However, in terms of procedures, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce should prepare a certificate for release. The relevant procedures have now been negotiated and completed by Gu Xinyi, chairman of the Miscellaneous Grain Association, and Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and have been handled accordingly. Therefore, Zhejiang rice and grain have been coming in steadily. As for Jiangsu Province, there has been no obstruction so far. Therefore, there is no need to panic about grain and rice in this city, and the price has also eased due to the large number of arrivals. Regarding the issue of grain control, in order to achieve unity, the central government will discuss unified measures by the Ministries of Finance, Industry, and Internal Affairs. According to news obtained by grain merchants in this city, a special grain management bureau will be established by the central government to be in charge of all matters such as grain purchase, warehousing, and transportation. It is expected to be realized soon.

According to Xinxin News, it was learned from the Miscellaneous Grain Industry that the sources of supply from various gangs have recently released rice from Zhejiang, and merchants are allowed to transport it freely to Shanghai after signing a pledge. As a result, the arrivals have suddenly increased. There were a total of 100 warehouses arriving the other day, accounting for more than 20,000 stones, and the people's hearts have settled. The market sales are sluggish, and the Jinqingyan and other gangs are not handling much goods, resulting in a situation of oversupply. Market prices have generally fallen, and if the source continues to surge, there will be a continued downward trend.

Chamber of Commerce Submits Urgent Request: Joint and Several Liability of Partnerships 119

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted another urgent request to the Legislative Yuan regarding the issue of joint and several liability of partnerships. The original petition stated, "Regarding the matter of submitting a request, concerning the amendment of the regulations on joint and several liability for partnership debts, your esteemed Yuan had adopted the opinions of the national business community and separately drafted a Commercial Registration Law to remedy the situation. However, because the draft was submitted in October of the 23rd year and opinions could not be unified, it has been stalled to this day and has not become a separate law for reference. Consequently, the requests of the national business community have not been fulfilled, and there is no hope of a satisfactory resolution to partnership debt disputes. From March of the 22nd year to June of this year, the affiliated chambers of commerce have sent telegrams urging a resolution three times and submitted petitions urging a resolution once. In July of this year, chambers of commerce from various provinces, cities, and counties attending a meeting in Shanghai also jointly submitted a petition urging a resolution. However, the draft has still not been opened for discussion and passed by your esteemed Yuan. The national business community believes that passing laws is the special prerogative of your esteemed Yuan. Part of the Commercial Registration Law pertains to matters already stipulated in the existing, still-valid General Rules for Merchants. Your esteemed Yuan has the authority to weigh whether there is a need to formulate a separate law. However, the origin of drafting a separate registration law stems from the issue of partnership liability. Therefore, the point regarding appropriately regulating this matter aligns your esteemed Yuan's view with business realities. Laws are the crystallization of public opinion, and merchants have been eagerly awaiting them for a long time. If there is no need to separately draft a Commercial Registration Law for the time being, then a remedy should urgently be devised regarding the joint and several liability of partnership debts to avoid being trapped in this difficult situation for a long time. It is appropriate to prepare a document and respectfully request your esteemed Yuan to review and approve it as appropriate for the public good."

Shanghai-Hankou Waterway Dries Up; Navigation Must Detour; Hankou Section of Tuanfeng and Yadan Islets to Be Navigated via Luohu Islet During Daytime; Waterway Obstruction Signals Established 120

According to a warning issued yesterday by the Customs Conservancy Department, navigation on the Yangtze River between Shanghai and Hankou requires detours due to the drying up and blockage of the Tuanfeng and Yadan Islets waterways in the Hankou section. The matter is important. Excerpts are as follows:

Waterway Dries Up: The shrinkage of the Yangtze River's water volume has not ceased. Although navigation between Shanghai and Hankou has been reduced in tonnage, obstacles continue to arise. According to a warning issued yesterday by the Customs Conservancy Department of this port, the Tuanfeng and Yadan Islets waterways in the Hankou section (both above Jiujiang) have dried up and become blocked. Therefore, all Yangtze River vessels traveling from Shanghai to Hankou or from Hankou to Shanghai must detour via Luohu Islet to the west and are only allowed to pass during daytime, with nighttime navigation prohibited.

Establishing Signals: The Customs has also established the following temporary signal methods for the Yangtze River's lower reaches due to the current shrinkage causing blockages. The following items have been approved by various ports along the Yangtze River's lower reaches and are to be widely known: Waterway Obstruction Signal universally used throughout the Yangtze River's lower reaches. If a waterway is narrow and difficult to navigate or blocked and impassable, hindering navigation safety, the original signal on the warning vessel marker at either end of the waterway will be removed and replaced with the following signals: (1) Daytime: Three black balls arranged vertically. (2) Nighttime: Three red lights arranged vertically.

Six Silk Factory Workers to Petition Party and Government Organs 121

The former Baohua Silk Weaving Factory, due to the unwarranted dismissal of a large number of workers and the factory director of Yucu Village severely beating a worker causing injury, led to successive strikes at six silk factories, including Fuxing and Tiancheng. More than a hundred representatives were sent yesterday morning to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the General Labor Union. Zhang Gongquan Talks About Guangzhou-Hankou and Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Connection; Ministry of Railways Has Not Yet Planned This Matter; External Rumors Are Purely Unfounded Speculation 123

Minister of Railways Zhang Jia'ao came to Shanghai from Beijing on official business. He went to Xiafei Road at 10:00 yesterday morning to mourn the death of Duan Qirui. In addition, due to military transport, traffic order is inevitably disrupted, resulting in repeated train crashes. The responsibility for the negligence cannot be determined. Only urge the authorities of the road to quickly install the necessary equipment to maintain road administration. Passenger trains between Guangzhou and Hankou run twice a week in each direction, and local passenger trains on each section run daily, he said.

Important News from the Chinese Ancient Coin Society 127

The Chinese Ancient Coin Society held its ninth research meeting yesterday, attended by more than 20 members including Zhang Shuxun, Yi Yugong, Cheng Wuquan, Yang Kailing, Hu Puan, Zhang Jiliang, Wu Jing'an, and Chen Ruzhai. The research topic was Song Huizong Coins. All agreed that the coins personally inscribed by Huizong were second to none in ancient and modern times. The skill of minting coins was no less than that of Xin Mang. His slender gold calligraphy style was spiritually exquisite. Huizong lived in a time of foreign invasion. Although he was not good at governing the country, he was good at making coins. He was not good at controlling the size of the coins, but he was good at controlling their inscriptions and making them aesthetically pleasing. When Cai Jing was Prime Minister, he minted Chongning coins that were cheap and overvalued. Poor people had difficulty eating, and the Grand View period still followed the same path. More than 100,000 people were accused of using politics to make money, so minting coins for the world should be carefully examined. In addition, the society's journal, Ancient Coins, issue number three, has been collected and arranged and will be published on the first of next month. It is reported that the main items include Weng Yiquan's unpublished manuscripts, as well as major works by Zhang Jiongbo, Zhang Shuxun, Zheng Jiaxiang, Cheng Wuquan, Ding Fubao, Yang Kailing, and others.

Bao Liwei and others, Russians who specialize in insuring cheap goods for huge fire insurance amounts, then storing them in foreign warehouses, and taking the opportunity to set fires in an attempt to obtain insurance compensation, again sent their fox tails, worth only more than 400 yuan, to Louis Moore Auction House on the 24th of last month. Accomplices posed as buyers and went to bid at the auction, deliberately raising the price to 6,000 yuan. After purchasing, they insured the five wooden boxes of fox tails for fire insurance of 6,000 yuan with the French-American Insurance Company and transported them to Longmao Foreign Warehouse, 77 Sichuan Road, for storage, thinking that after a period of time, the

Arson Pieces

Installed in the box would automatically explode, causing a fire, and they could sit back and reap the benefits. Unexpectedly, this plan was known to the patrol room in advance, so when Bao Liwei and Ke Nele were transporting the boxes into the warehouse, they were intercepted on the spot by Detective Chief Feng Zhiming, Liu Shaokui, Detective She Fu Tang, and others, and then five more accomplices were arrested and sent to the First Special District District Court. The facts of the case were recorded in this newspaper. Now, according to the detailed investigation by the handling detectives, the result is that one of them, Ma Jinggao Weisigan,

Definitely Not Related

Yesterday afternoon, he and the other six Russians were escorted to the court. Court President Qian Hongye conducted the interrogation. The patrol room lawyer Ru Baoyi requested that Ma Jinggao Weisigan be released, while for Ke Nele, Shiliwei Aopeile Paner Sigan, Liwei Sigan, Weisigan, and Xier Xuhau, they were

Prosecuted on Two Counts

Of endangering public safety and fraud, because the defendants' behavior was dangerous as a method and aimed at fraud. In front of the court, the judge ordered Ma Jinggao Weisigan to be released. Then, Lawyer Ru stated the relationship of the six defendants to the case, saying that the first and second defendants transported the wooden boxes to the Samoa warehouse on the 24th of last month. In the residences of these two people, they found the bill issued by Louis Moore for the auction of leather goods, the warehouse list issued by Longmao, and the machine parts for arson. The explosive power of this machine was

Examined by Experts

And a report was made. The expert can also come to court to testify. As for the third and fourth defendants, they jointly manufactured the arson machine. In the home of the fifth defendant, leather goods and remaining machine parts were also hidden. The sixth defendant was one of the people who went to the auction house to bid when the leather goods were auctioned. The price of 6,000 yuan was also set by him. Now, the first, second, and third defendants have all confessed to

Intending to Set Fire

However, the remaining three defendants are still cunning. Various documents seized and the arson machine that was partially dismantled by the patrol room were presented to the court. After viewing the evidence, it was decided to have the handling detective report the process of solving the case. Then, Wu Zimei and other employees of Longmao Warehouse testified that the Russians had sent wooden boxes to the warehouse for storage in succession since May 18 of this year, totaling five times. Then, Judge Qian interrogated the defendants one by one and ordered them to await a renewed trial at a later date.

Weather Turns Cold, Heavy Fog in the City This Morning 144

Lowest Temperature Only Slightly Above 30 Degrees, Traffic Considerably Hindered in Fog

Since the Beginning of Winter (立冬) on the 7th, the weather in this city has turned cold. The lowest temperature daily has been only around 17 or 18 degrees. This morning, heavy fog appeared. The details are as follows:

Weather: Turning Cold

Since the rain on the 1st, the weather in this city has completely reversed its previous warmth. After the Beginning of Winter on the 7th, the weather has become even colder. According to the observatory, the lowest temperature in the past few days has been only 37 or 38 degrees, presenting the appearance of winter. At the same time, the west wind blows frequently. Autumn clothes are put away, and nothing less than fur robes is sufficient to keep warm.

This Morning: Foggy

After daybreak this morning, there was also heavy fog. Objects at a slight distance were not clearly visible. Vehicles on the main roads moved slowly. Many ships entering the port in the early morning were obstructed and had to anchor outside the port. The fog gradually dissipated after 9:00 AM, and traffic resumed.

American's Manslaughter of Rickshaw Puller: Case File Transferred to City Government; American Assessor's Office States It Will Handle Case According to Law 145

The case of American national Gillis Martin beating to death rickshaw puller Sun Weiyu near Yu’s residence in the new western district of the Southern City on the morning of the 4th of this month: the perpetrator Martin has already been handed over by the Public Security Bureau to the American Consulate and detained in the Western Jail of the Public Works Department on Ward Road. The deceased's body was also inspected by the local court, which determined that he died by falling into the riverbank and drowning after being injured. An autopsy report was attached to the case file. The prosecutor in charge of examining the case, Kong Xianglin, believes that the case file should be compiled and submitted to the city government for handling negotiations. Therefore, yesterday he summoned witnesses Xue Zhengfu, Jiang Yu, and the deceased's brothers Sun Weifang and Sun Weiyu to the case to hear their testimonies and the plaintiffs' claims. Written records were taken to be attached to the case file for transfer to the city government for handling.

Furthermore, regarding the case of American national Martin beating rickshaw puller Sun Weiyu to death, the U.S. Consulate in Shanghai attaches great importance to it and has telegraphed the details to the U.S. government. A new judge, Watson (transliteration), has been specially appointed to come to China to be responsible for the trial of this case. Mr. Watson is currently awaiting a ship in San Francisco. At 9:00 AM yesterday, the City Public Security Bureau specially dispatched Inspector Zhao Bojun, accompanied by a Western officer from the Central Police Station, to the American Consulate to meet with Prosecutor Trumbull of the Assessor's Office and Judge Hamke to inquire about the date of the trial, so as to be prepared for negotiations at that time. They also inquired about Martin's degree of intoxication after the rickshaw ride and the details of the assault. Mr. Hamke responsibly stated that if the U.S. government considers Martin guilty, he will be tried according to American law, without partiality or leniency. However, since the new judge Watson cannot arrive for the time being, a well-reputed American expatriate in Shanghai who is familiar with the law and the situation in Shanghai will be selected to be primarily responsible for handling the case first.

Beijing Apartments,

Room 12. Previously released after translation.

He was immediately arrested

and taken back to the police station for strict interrogation. According to Zhang, he was a servant at the Guo residence at No. 582 Rue de la Lousinne. that Zhang was employed,

Forging Small Champagne Tickets: Police Investigate and Prosecute; Mastermind Xie Rongqing Flees; Eight Defendants Await Sentencing 147

Chief Detective of the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Rice Ziqing, Zhang Xiaolin, and Western Detective Luo Si previously learned that someone was privately counterfeiting small champagne tickets for the race meeting to be held at the Race Club on the 10th of this month and selling them in the city. They began to investigate and confirmed the information. On the 1st of this month, they arrested the suspects (1) Feng Qishan, (2) Xu Weibing, (4) Qiu Xianfu, (4) Zhang Xianggui, (5) Yin Yangchun, (6) Chen Sentang, (7) Zhao Bingsheng, and (8) Yu Luruo, and confiscated the counterfeit champagne tickets

more than three thousand sheets

from the Tongchun Printing Shop at No. 7 Cuijia Lane, Fumin Road in the Southern City.

Another fifty fake tickets each were found on the first and second defendant. They were sent to the First Special Court with a request for detention. The circumstances were previously reported in this newspaper. This morning, Judge Qian Hongye continued the trial in the First Criminal Court. Police lawyer Ru Bao Yi prosecuted the defendants under Article 210 of the Criminal Law, which punishes forgery. Defendants Zhao Bingsheng and Yu Luruo hired lawyers Yu Enliang and Wu Peng to defend them. Lawyer Ru then presented the investigation of the case, saying

the most important aspect

pertained to the sixth defendant, Chen Sentang. Chen and Xie Rongqing, who is at large, were previously colleagues on a ship that traveled between Hankou and Shanghai. On the 19th of last month, Xie conceived the idea of counterfeiting champagne tickets from the race club and entrusted Chen to handle it, totaling four thousand tickets, for which he was willing to pay four yuan per hundred tickets. The next day, the 20th, Xie and Chen met at the Yilinchun Tea House on Jiujiang Road. Xie handed over genuine champagne tickets, from No. 1936 to No. 1932,

and asked Chen to print them

in the same way. After they were printed, they were to be sent to Yongyu Trading Company, No. 55 Daijia Port, Hankou. They then parted ways. Chen then went to the Weisheng Engraving Shop at No. 4 Lane, Rue Belleville in the French Concession and entrusted the seventh and eighth defendants to make zinc plates. The seventh defendant was the accountant of the engraving shop, and the eighth defendant was the owner of the shop. They made three zinc plates, costing five yuan. After Chen obtained the zinc plates, he went to Gongyu Paper Shop on Tiantong Road on October 26th and

paid five yuan

for two hundred sheets of paper. He then went to the Tongchun Printing Shop at No. 7 Cuijia Lane, Fumin Road in the Southern City, opened by Chuan Tongchun, and negotiated printing procedures. It was agreed that the printing fee would be four yuan per thousand sheets for four thousand sheets. Chuan ordered the workers, the fourth and fifth defendants, to do the printing. After the printing was completed, Chen Sentang found that there were still shortcomings. He then entrusted the seventh and eighth defendants of the engraving shop to counterfeit the Race Club's seal and stamp it on the tickets.

The matter was completed.

Chen entrusted the third defendant, Qiu Xianfu, to sell the tickets in Nantung and other places outside of the city, for five yuan per hundred tickets. In Shanghai, he entrusted the second defendant, Xu Weibing, to sell them for seven yuan per hundred tickets. Xu then entrusted the first defendant, Feng Qishan, to sell fifty tickets for nine yuan. Therefore, when the first and second defendants were arrested, ninety tickets each were found on them. He then submitted the confiscated items to the court for investigation. When questioned, most of the defendants admitted to the charges. After mutual arguments by the two lawyers, the court ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and await sentencing on the 11th of this month.

Su Keming's Car Kills Girl 149

At 3:15 PM the day before yesterday, the only daughter, Xiaomeitou, also known as Guizhen, 14 years old, of the widow Lu Gu from Lujiadun, 93rd Xiang, Qingdeng Temple Northwest, Maqiao Town, Shangsong Road, was returning home from watching a play in Maqiao. While walking on Shangsong Road, west of Maqiao Station, a private car owned by Su Keming, a native of Songjiang with license number 8898 and Shanghai license number 3213, was speeding from east to west. Xiaomeitou Lu was unable to avoid it and was knocked to the ground, head east and feet west, her brains splattered. She died on the spot. The driver, seeing the disaster he had caused, immediately sped off to the north. The villagers at the scene reported it to the Maqiao Third Substation. Inspector Ma Wenbin, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched Police Chief Jiang Dengxian and police to investigate. They then pursued the car to Chedun, east of Huayang Bridge, where they found the car, which had stopped on the side of the road due to mechanical damage. Su Keming and the driver had already fled. Yesterday, the Shanghai Local Court dispatched a prosecutor and inspectors to the scene for inspection. The inspectors confirmed that the deceased girl, named Lu Xiaomeitou, had been killed by a car. The body was handed over to the mother, Lu Gu, to prepare a coffin for burial, pending the arrest of the suspect and investigation.

Shipping Industry Association Appeals for Strict Suppression of Pirates to Eradicate Banditry and Protect Merchants 151

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association sent telegrams to the Third District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, the Coastal Patrol Department of the Navy, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the Songhu Garrison Command regarding the robbery of the Baohua ship: "According to a report from our member, the Ping An Shipping Company, our company's Baohua ship departed from Pier No. 8 in the Southern City at 5:00 PM on the 6th of this month. At 7:00 PM, outside of Wusongkou, more than a dozen robbers speaking a strong northern accent suddenly opened fire. They first went to the escort police room and confiscated the guns, then opened fire in the accounting room, robbing more than 400 yuan of ticket sales and money entrusted by customers. They then moved the upper-class passengers, along with the tea room staff, down to the lower class and drove everyone to the front lower class, where they began to search and rob all the money and neatly arranged clothing they had on them. Around 11:00 PM, a sailboat came alongside and took the 16 pirates away. The location of the incident was near Liangsha and Ougang Port in Chongming. It was discovered that one passenger was shot and wounded by the pirates, and a package of cargo and a cylinder head from the engine room were taken away, rendering the ship unable to operate. They immediately dropped anchor and waited until 6:00 AM the next morning before sailing back to Shanghai, arriving at Pier No. 8 in the Southern City at 11:30 AM on the morning of the 7th. We urgently reported to the affiliated association to forward the report to the military and police agencies, requesting strict investigation, recovery of the stolen goods, and punishment. We are now reporting the situation and earnestly request that you promptly conduct a strict investigation, bring the perpetrators to justice, eradicate banditry, and protect merchants. We are deeply grateful. The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association respectfully states."
