Mathematics Magazine, Second Issue Published. The Mathematics Magazine, edited and published by the Chinese Mathematical Society, is written by famous mathematicians in the country. The content focuses on the discussion of basic concepts and the consultation of teaching methods. There are four issues per year, sold by Commercial Press bookstores in various places. Since its publication, it has been highly valued by the academic community in the country. The second issue was published on November 1st. The main articles include Fan Huiguo's Classification of Functions, Zhang Yongzhi's Research on the Yangli Jiazi, Zhu Gongjin's Commemoration of Riemann, and German Knopp's Infinite Series and Dedekind's On the Meaning of Numbers. These are world-renowned works with profound relationships to the foundations of mathematics. Various countries have translated them, but our country has not yet done so. Recently, Gu Fanwu and Zhu Gongjin have translated and annotated them separately. In addition, Wang Liansong's Error in the Solution of the Three Major Problems of Geometry points out the errors in the solution. There is also an article on the Interpretation of Existence, which also addresses this issue. All those who are interested in mathematics should have a copy.

Weather Report 164

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday, stating that the weather around Shandong is sunny and cold with southwest to northwest winds. There are southwest winds in the Yellow River basin. There are northwest to north winds in the upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River. The weather in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River is sunny and quite cold with northeast to southeast winds. There is light fog in the morning. The weather in the East China Sea and Taiwan is cloudy with strong northeast winds. The hurricane in the Pacific Ocean is clearly moving northward. Its center at 2:00 p.m. was within 120 miles of 20 degrees north latitude and 133 degrees east longitude. The wind force is unknown. In addition, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 p.m. yesterday was 66.7 degrees and the lowest was 42.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 69.3 degrees and the lowest was 45.1 degrees.

Letter to the Editor 165

To the Editor:

I recently read the Shanghai news columns in the Shen Bao, Xin Bao, Min Bao, and Da Gong Bao of the 9th of this month, which reported that the Shanghai Recreation Association opposed the Telegraph Bureau's restriction on the broadcasting time of ten programs. The facts are quite different and are completely one-sided, which seems to have other purposes. Our bureau was ordered to restrict the broadcasting time of these recreation programs because the lyrics of these programs are obscene and absurd, which hinders social development. Therefore, we first imposed passive restrictions to clear the airwaves. We are now actively working to enrich the content to promote social education and improve the effectiveness of broadcasting. We have always admired your newspaper's efforts in cultural construction, detailed analysis, and fair criticism. Therefore, we are sending this letter to the editor, and we ask that you publish this letter so that we can make improvements.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications

General Situation of Industrial and Commercial Changes in Shanghai in July and August of This Year, Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce (37) 168

— Edited by China

In July of this year, Shanghai's industry and commerce slightly improved after the summer festival and the half-year settlement period. However, the exhausted and sluggish phenomenon continued to exist. In the financial industry, the opposition between commercial banks and state-owned banks became increasingly acute. A portion of the commercial banks with weaker foundations mostly adopted a defensive stance, contracting and gradually stagnating. Therefore, the phenomenon of capital concentration became more and more obvious. In the industrial sector, the decline followed a straight line, with little sign of improvement. As for the sales business and consumer business, which are at the heart of the market, although the number of new creations was considerable, the number of bankruptcies doubled. Moreover, there were many cases of reorganization or liquidation within three or four months of operation. This is because the purchasing power of the market has not increased, and the turnover of finance is still stagnant. In August of this year, Shanghai's industry and commerce remained relatively stable in the general downward trend. Although the number of new creations decreased, the decrease in the number of closures was even greater. Therefore, relatively speaking, it can be regarded as a turning point. The reasons for this are probably two: one is that the changes in sales firms in this month were relatively moderate, and the other is that the manufacturing industry has shown a trend of prosperity. The only difference is that the chaotic state under the category of special undertakings has become more serious than before. Now, the statistics of various changes in July and August will be compared with the previous two months (ie, May and June) and the corresponding period last year, as shown in the table below.

The distribution of the various changes in July and August of this year listed in the previous table among the various industries is as follows:

Municipal Physical Education School Invites Director Pan to Speak 181

To Indicate the True Meaning of Promoting Sports, To Break the General Misconceptions

The Municipal Physical Education School of this city invited Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau to give a speech at the memorial week held at 9:00 a.m. yesterday. The general idea was that physical education is education, and education cannot be divided. It not only cultivates knowledge, but also exercises the body. The general public thinks that physical education is what people in physical education schools pursue, and people in physical education schools also think that they are specialized in physical education and that there is no need to study other knowledge. Therefore, the meaning of education is divided, which is a very big mistake. Moreover, the general schools treat athletes differently, even giving them rich food and clothing, and the homework is more relaxed. Raising some athletes to win championships when the school starts the sports meet is tantamount to treating athletes as toys and tools, which is also a very big mistake. Therefore, we must break this misconception. We not only seek physical health, but also psychological health. Although we study physical education, we also attach importance to knowledge, because the meaning of education is to make a person whole and upward, not just to complete the training of the body. Especially the students of our Municipal Physical Education School should recognize this meaning to correct the mistakes of the general public.

City No. 1 Stadium Chess News 182

In view of the fact that people who generally exercise are very interested in chess, City No. 1 Stadium has specially organized the first chess competition to fulfill the wishes of the public. Registration is scheduled to begin yesterday and will close on the 23rd of this month. The competition time is from 7:00 p.m. every day, which does not hinder the exercise of professional and practicing sports from all walks of life. The method is to take the complex cycle system. Depending on the number of participants, the lottery will be divided into several groups, each with a single cycle competition. One person with the best score will be recorded and combined into one group, and then a single cycle competition will be held. The three people with the best scores will be the winners of the first, second, and third places in the Class A category. The one person with the best scores among the first place and below in the group cycle competition will be drawn again to form a group and hold a single cycle competition. The three people with the best scores will be the first, second, and third place winners in the Class B category. During the competition, the spirit of the New Life Movement will be used to eliminate the bad habits of the old game of arching, such as smoking cigarettes and untidy clothes, which are not allowed to enter the room for competition. Those who have a lack of humility in their words and attitudes will also be subject to considerable penalties, and attention will also be paid to observing the time and obeying the judgment.

Comparison of Tuition Fees for Private Schools in Various Provinces and Cities for Improvement 183

The following is a summary of the tuition fees charged by private schools across the country throughout the year, and whether they have been improved, based on the results of the Ministry of Education's survey in the 24th year of the Republic of China. (Explanation) Improvement refers to the use of school textbooks. Non-improvement refers to the non-use of textbooks. With the exception of Xinjiang and Weihaiwei, where there are no private schools, and Hunan and Xikang, where the number of private schools has not been reported (many private schools in Hunan have been improved separately), of the 1,558,000 private schools that have been reported, those that have been improved account for slightly less than 47%, and those that have not been improved account for slightly more than 52%. This is the situation in the 24th year of the Republic of China. Since the implementation of compulsory education and the training of private school teachers in various provinces, the number of private schools that have been improved since the 25th year of the Republic of China should have increased compared to before.

General Situation of Rural Education in the Country 184

(Nanjing, 8th) The Central Agricultural Experiment Institute has now released the general situation of rural education in the country based on the surveys of agricultural information reporters from various provinces. According to the survey, the percentages of various rural education institutions are: Public primary schools 47%, Private primary schools 17.5%, Private schools 30.3%, Social education institutions 14.2%, Vocational education institutions 0.3%, Middle schools 0.7%. The percentages of the number of students in various rural education institutions to the total number of students are: Public primary schools 60.2%, Private primary schools 18.3%, Private schools 19.2%, Vocational education institutions 0.4%, Middle schools 0.9%. The percentages of the funds for various rural education institutions are: Public primary schools 96.0%, Social education institutions 3.0%, Vocational education institutions 1.0%. The funds for private primary schools, private schools, and middle schools are unknown. Among rural social education, night schools for the public are the most developed. Among rural vocational education, vocational schools are the most developed, followed by agricultural schools. In rural education at all levels, early primary schools are the most developed, and junior high schools are more numerous among middle schools. In terms of public and private schools, public schools account for 76% and private schools account for 24%. Among rural primary school teachers, graduates of junior high schools and normal schools are the most numerous. On average, each rural primary school has 2.4 teachers.

General Situation of National Education (5) 186

— Lei Zhen

Our country has complete libraries, but not many. The National Peking Library can be considered our country's only complete library. The National Central Library, which is being planned, is also roughly taking shape and is now open for reading. Furthermore, a site for the library has been decided, and construction of a grand-scale library will begin soon. The Oriental Library, run by the Commercial Press, is very rich in content and has many treasures, but unfortunately, it was destroyed in the January 28th Incident. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there are a total of 1,634 libraries in the country, including 48 provincial and municipal libraries, 1,260 county and municipal libraries, and 363 private libraries. Radio education, through wireless broadcasting, allows countless people, near and far, to listen. It transmits news very quickly and is very useful for implementing social education. If every village and city in our country could be universally equipped with radios, and educational institutions could broadcast at fixed times on radio stations, it would be very effective for imparting knowledge, disseminating government information, or broadcasting music and drama to satisfy the public's spiritual needs. Once a foreign war breaks out, it can also serve as a powerful tool for transmitting news and unifying the people's will. The Ministry of Education has been implementing this type of radio education since the 24th year of the Republic (1935), ordering all provincial and municipal secondary schools and mass education centers to equip themselves with radios. It stipulated that at least one-third of secondary schools and mass education centers must have radios installed by December of the 24th year. By December of the 26th year (1937), all secondary schools and mass education centers across the country were to be equipped with radios. Last summer, a training class for broadcasting personnel was also established to train personnel to manage radios, who were then assigned to various provinces and cities to carry out radio education. On the one hand, it was stipulated that experts be hired to broadcast at fixed times each week, with secondary schools as the target on Wednesdays, and the general public as the target four times a week. This year, it is still continuing without interruption. Now, a Radio Education Committee has been organized to study broadcasting issues and plan the promotion of radio education and methods to improve the efficiency of radio education.

Film education: Film is a powerful tool for modern education. If all kinds of knowledge and skills can be made into films and shown to the public, it will be a very powerful tool for enlightening the people, disseminating government information, reforming customs and habits, and unifying the people's will. The Ministry of Education is now working with other relevant agencies to produce educational films, and is ordering educational institutions in various provinces and cities to install projectors to implement film education. Recently, a Film Education Committee has been organized, whose duties are (1) to plan the selection and exchange of foreign educational films, (2) to plan the production of educational films, (3) to plan the promotion of film education, and (4) to study various issues related to the implementation of film education, in order to improve the efficiency of film education. A training class for electro-educational personnel is also being held in the capital to train broadcasting and film education personnel for various provinces and cities, and it has already been in session for many days. The important social education undertakings have already been described separately. As for the total number of social education institutions in the country, according to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there are a total of 97,591, including 45,951 school-type social education institutions and 51,640 general social education institutions. The number of students in school-type social education institutions is 1,496,986.

5. General Situation of Mongolian and Tibetan Education

Border education in our country lags behind that of the interior. In addition to slightly learning Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui scripts for religious needs, the people know nothing else. As a result, the culture is extremely backward. The National Government, recognizing the mistakes of the past, established the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Department in the Ministry of Education in the 18th year of the Republic (1929), dedicated to managing Mongolian, Tibetan, Hui, and Miao education affairs. Over the years, progress has been made. In the 24th year of the Republic (1935), the Central Government allocated 500,000 yuan for border education, designating various border provinces to conduct Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui education. The Hui elementary schools and Tibetan elementary schools that Gansu Province is planning to establish have already opened in September of this year. Yunnan Province has established three Miao normal schools and 34 Miao elementary schools. Guizhou Province has established one Miao normal school and two Miao elementary schools. Ningxia Province has established one Mongolian and Hui normal school, three Mongolian elementary schools, and two Hui elementary schools. In Suiyuan Province, one National Mongolian Banner Normal School has been established and one or two Mongolian Banner primary and secondary schools have been subsidized. Chahar Province has jointly established a Mongolian normal school with Suiyuan. Xinjiang has established one Hui normal school and more than 1,200 Hui elementary schools. Furthermore, Xikang and Qinghai have also respectively subsidized and restored Mongolian and Tibetan normal classes and many Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui elementary schools. This year, the Central Government is still allocating 500,000 yuan for border education, and the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees is subsidizing an additional 200,000 yuan. The Ministry of Education, together with the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, will formulate implementation plans and implement them accordingly. The following items must be handled this year:

1. Consolidate the Mongolian, Tibetan, Hui, and Miao education undertakings that have already been carried out in the previous year, and increase the number of grades. Establish more normal schools and elementary schools in important places, and gradually carry out vocational education and social education undertakings.

2. Encourage Mongolian, Tibetan, Hui, and Miao students to advance to specialized schools above the undergraduate level in the interior. In recent years, due to the Central Government's active promotion of preferential treatment for Mongolian and Tibetan students to advance to higher education, significant results have been achieved. This year, an additional 5,000 yuan has been allocated specifically to subsidize young people from the border areas to advance to specialized schools in the country. 3. Compile and print bilingual Chinese-Tibetan elementary school textbooks and literacy textbooks for the masses, proceeding in the following four steps: (1) The eight volumes of Chinese-Mongolian bilingual national language textbooks and four volumes of short-term elementary school textbooks that have been compiled and translated by the Ministry of Education will be printed and distributed for use in August. (2) The Ministry of Education will hire Tibetan and Hui language experts to translate the short-term Tibetan and Hui language elementary school textbooks first, and print and distribute them for use by the end of October. (3) The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission will compile and translate three types of literacy textbooks for civilians in Chinese, Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui languages, each with four volumes, which will be reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Education and printed and distributed for use. All the above books will take Mandarin Chinese as the main body, and will be accompanied by translations and annotations in Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui languages for comparison and reference. However, the Miao people only have language but no writing, so it is planned to use the Mandarin phonetic alphabet to facilitate teaching. (4) Continue to send personnel to inspect the Mongolian, Tibetan, Hui, and Miao education situation in various border provinces. The inspection area is tentatively planned to include the "Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia," "Gansu, Qinghai, Xinjiang," and "Xikang, Yunnan, Guizhou" three major regions, including nine provinces, with one person assigned to each region to conduct inspections and discuss everything with the local officials in charge.

3. Other

The above has briefly discussed the national education situation, including elementary, secondary, higher, social, Mongolian, and Tibetan education. Now, I will briefly discuss the national education funding situation to conclude. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the funding for elementary education was 10,680,5851 yuan, the funding for secondary education was 56,644,838 yuan, the funding for higher education was 33,574,896 yuan, and the funding for social education was 17,487,812 yuan, totaling 214,513,397 yuan. The above refers to both public and private institutions. In recent years, there have been increases, but there are no accurate statistics available for reporting. End. (The End)

Ministry of Education Gives Preferential Treatment to Miao Yi Students 187

Those who come to the Central Government or various provinces to study shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for Mongolian and Tibetan students. An instruction is issued to all public and private universities to comply.

The Ministry of Education recently issued an instruction to all public and private universities in the country, in order to give preferential treatment to Miao Yi students who come to study at the Central Government or provinces. The case was approved by the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, General Character No. 4950, and states that the Southwest Yi Ethnic Culture Promotion Association Nanjing General Assembly has requested to follow the revised regulations for the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students, to ensure that Yi children can advance to higher education, etc. It is hereby requested to review and implement accordingly. It is hereby approved that the Miao Yi ethnic groups are also border ethnic groups, and their distribution area is extremely wide. Their cultural level is lower than that of the Mongolian and Tibetan ethnic groups. At this time of promoting border education, all Miao Yi students who come to the Central Government and various provinces to study should be given special preferential treatment to show encouragement. It is hereby tentatively approved to handle the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students in accordance with the provisions of the various articles of the regulations for the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students, which were revised and promulgated on June 25th of the 24th year of the Republic (1935), No. 8603 by this Department. Those who are recommended by the recommending agency or who impersonate Miao Yi students shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 9 and 10 of the regulations. In addition to the reply, a copy of the original consultation and the revised regulations for the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students are hereby urgently forwarded for compliance. This order is issued.

Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Special Issue

The Current Situation of Nursing and Nurse Education in Japan 200

— Hua Xiren (Described), Zhang Jingmin (Recorded)

After passing through the venereal disease department, you can see many women undergoing electrotherapy. Driven by curiosity, I asked the doctors inside about the names of the diseases. These doctors asked the nurses, who then asked the director to find out. Soon, you see a towering building, which is the most beautiful nursing school in East Asia. The facilities inside are very perfect, and there are many technical testing sites for nursing students: When each student enters the school, they must first be taught how to bathe and how to wash bakelite utensils. We know that Japanese people are not very smart, and they can never make coffee.

Nurse Education and Everything About Nurses

The education systems and educational situations in England, America, China, and Japan are roughly the same: However, nurse education in Japan is entirely handled by experts, taking a division of labor system, unlike our country's professors who take on multiple roles and play solo acts. This educational method is indeed their advantage: It is worthy of our adoption, but they also have their shortcomings, that is, what they learn is not what they use, and learning and application cannot be integrated, so their skills are not very skilled. However, they are absolutely obedient to doctors in terms of both technical aspects and other public and private aspects, as long as the doctors instruct them.

Hospitals in Tokyo

The Japanese call nurses "Kango," and they used to be called "Kangofu." As for the name "Kango," it originated in Japan. We can determine from the vulgarity of this name that Japanese education will not surpass that of China. Within the territory of Tokyo, there are two largest medical institutions with the largest scale: one is the Tokyo Imperial University Hospital, and the other is the Tongren Hospital. In addition to Tokyo Imperial University, each of these two treatment institutions is attached to a nursing school. Of course, one is the Tongren Hospital Nursing School, and the other is the Tokyo Imperial University Attached Nursing School. Among them, the Tongren Nursing School is more magnificent and has more economic resources than the Imperial University Nursing School; because Tongren Hospital is co-sponsored by people from various countries, the scale is great and the economy is very sufficient. In Tokyo, it is one of the leading hospitals, and the general situation is roughly the same as that of the Peking Union Medical College Hospital.

Record of Sightings in Tongren Hospital

The principal of a nursing school at Tongren once told us, "If we compare the nursing education in China and Japan, of course China is very advanced, but why is Japan not advanced? There are three major reasons: one, Japanese people can't wash dishes, two, they can't bathe, and three, they can't make coffee. However, what about the Chinese? They can be said to be good at these things," According to what she said, there is indeed a lot of sarcasm in it. Is it possible that Chinese people are only good at doing these lowly things? It is a bit too much and not close to the facts. As for the three things that Japanese people can't do, perhaps they are true. This is what happened when we visited Tongren Hospital.

The career prospects for nurses in Japan are very good, such as in public health, hospital nursing, and private clinics. When it comes to the level of general public health education, it is of course higher than in China. According to reason, Japan's health facilities are undoubtedly higher than those in China, but the fact is the opposite. China's health facilities are more complete than Japan's. As for the level of Japanese nurses entering school, a primary school graduation is enough, and the period of study is three and a half years. The situation in all classes is far inferior to that in China; however, each nurse is very united with other nurses in China, like a group: so when we walk on the streets, we can see the signs of the Nursing Association posted in places where people gather. If a hospital needs nurses, they can contact the association, and the association will introduce them according to the length of time the unemployed have been unemployed, or sometimes advertise for external recruitment.

During this very special period in our country, the Japanese government is paying special attention to nurse education, and almost every citizen has to go through this step. Moreover, at present, nurse education and wartime first aid have been included in national defense education, and are designated as compulsory courses for every citizen during the period of nurse education. If we carefully analyze Japanese nurse education, we can see at a glance from the surface that their level is very low, but the actual work they do is very large and many; it focuses on practice.

There have only been two male nurses in all of Tokyo from the past to the present. They both serve as mental illness nurses. As for the reason for needing male nurses, there are three: one is the social background, two is the economic situation, and three is the social need. Sometimes there is a surplus of nurses, and sometimes there are not enough nurses to use. This phenomenon of mismatch between supply and demand is rare in Japan.

Explanation of Blood Transfusion (Part 1) 201

— Jiang Yisheng

On October 5th, the Shen Bao published an article in which lawyer Yuan proposed a suggestion to the Bar Association to request an explanation from the authorities as to whether blood transfusion is illegal. While the intention of helping the poor and supporting the rich, and prioritizing life and health, is commendable, it is based on a lack of understanding and purely personal emotions. Therefore, I have some objections. The original text has two main points: (1) Any body from which blood is drawn will immediately suffer damage to its health. Voluntarily accepting injury is no different from suicide, and there is guilt in instigating or assisting others to commit suicide. (2) Buying and selling blood is of no practical benefit to the patient. Even if it is beneficial, the purpose is to make the rich stronger and the poor weaker, the rich live and the poor die. (Omission in the middle)—Occasionally, when a patient loses too much blood, in order to avoid the greater of two evils, they choose to transfuse blood of the same type from within the same clan. This practice exists in Western countries, but making a profit from it is absolutely prohibited. Now, I will provide a point-by-point explanation as follows:

(1) (A) The average blood volume of an adult is 4.5 liters. A blood transfusion volume of 200 to 800 cubic centimeters (cc) causes the blood donor a loss that is completely restored within a few hours, and will definitely not lead to anemia or damage to health. This is because the metabolism of blood is constantly occurring. After a small loss, the blood-producing organs are stimulated and work faster, producing blood more quickly.

(B) Conditions for blood transfusion: (A) For the blood donor: there is absolutely no harm to the blood donor's health, and it is beneficial to the recipient's ailing body. Therefore, the physical examination must be absolutely strict. (1) Only young, strong people with no suspicion of infectious diseases are suitable. (2) The blood type identification must be carefully done. If the blood types match, the recipient will accept it without any problems. If they do not match, agglutination will occur, leading to death in an instant. (3) Once the blood donor's blood type is known and the physical condition is suitable, and they are registered at the hospital, they must maintain their good health. This is because blood type is fixed from birth, but good health cannot be guaranteed to be constant. All things that damage good health should be strictly warned against and carefully protected. (4) Blood transfusion should not be performed repeatedly within a considerable period.

(B) For the recipient: the doctor makes a purely scientific judgment that there is an absolute need, such as "life depends on it, death without it," such as (1) simple acute excessive blood loss, life hanging by a thread, the body's own blood has no time for metabolism and lacks the ability. If the doctor uses physiological saline to help, although the quantity can be increased, the quality is too thin, and they must use the blood of others to bring the dead back to life and achieve miraculous results instantly. (2) Anemia caused by disease or (3) when severe illnesses cannot be treated with medication, blood not only nourishes the body but is also the main base for the body's fight against disease. Blood transfusion increases nutrition and can also be seen as a fresh force. The body's own blood gets some external help, accelerating metabolism and strengthening resistance.

Overall, blood transfusion is absolutely harmless and beneficial to the blood donor. (1) If you have a hidden illness, you can find out during the physical examination and not miss the opportunity for treatment. (2) Your blood type becomes known. If you suffer a serious injury or critical illness, you can immediately become a recipient, saving the time-consuming blood testing procedure and avoiding endangering your life. (3) You must maintain your good health, at least to the extent that you dare not frequent prostitutes or contract venereal diseases, so as not to lose your eligibility to be a blood donor. So, where is the injury? Where is the suicide? Lightly accusing doctors of criminal responsibility for inciting or assisting suicide is illogical, fabricating crimes, and should not be done! I will imitate his tone and say that blood transfusion saves lives. Obstructing blood transfusion is obstructing saving lives. Obstructing saving lives is no different from killing. Killers are guilty. However, I definitely do not want to say such things. The author's intention is kind. As for hospitals seeking people to register in advance, the recipient's need is a matter of life and death, at a critical juncture. Sometimes the condition is so critical that one person's blood transfusion is not enough to save a life, and multiple people must share the responsibility and change people repeatedly. Examining the physical condition and testing blood types on the spot is not possible within the time constraints. The meaning of preparing ahead is easily understood. Someone might say you are indeed good at arguing, because I have heard of people fainting from blood transfusion in Peiping. I say, yes, yes, this is a psychological effect, not a blood loss effect! Chinese people have always valued blood, especially men. Women's psychology should be more fragile than men's. Why don't we hear of women fainting when they have their periods? It is a common occurrence. Nor have we heard of healthy women becoming bloodless because of excessive menstruation. This is metabolism. This can also prove that blood transfusion is harmless to health, without a doubt. With the psychology of valuing blood, selling it one day will initially cause terror and ultimately regret and anger, and then they might faint. And there are people who faint even when they see a little bit of their own blood flowing. When I tested people for Wassermann reaction, taking only 4 cc of blood, three people fainted: two men and one woman.

(2) Practical benefits for the patient: Just looking at Shanghai alone, the hospitals use blood transfusion to revive the dying and restore flesh to bones. These are ironclad facts that can be verified. The original text says "of no practical benefit to the patient," and the next sentence immediately follows with "even if it is beneficial." How well does Lawyer Yuan use the word "even"! I speculate that his conscience when writing could not directly deny the miraculous achievements of blood transfusion. He hesitated slightly and then added the word "even." Wonderful! "Even setting aside blood transfusion itself and talking about the rich and poor, the rich are rich in wealth but poor in blood, and the poor are poor in wealth but rich in blood. Using surplus to make up for deficiencies, mutually benefiting each other is fair and just. Measured by the meaning of obligations and rights, what is wrong with it? Moreover, blood donors save people from the brink of death, which is great benevolence and righteousness. Benevolence and righteousness bring profit, and all three are beautiful. If Mencius were resurrected today, he would not have the lament 'Why must you speak of profit?'" As for the situation in Western countries, I will briefly mention two things to prove it. (1) There are many American and British soldiers stationed in Shanghai who voluntarily sell blood and register at hospitals. The original author can go to various hospitals to investigate or even request on-site observation to prove it. (2) My friend Dr. Zhu Gonghong received his doctorate and transfused blood many times while studying in the United States, earning 20 to 100 US dollars each time. The American and British military are strict in discipline and pay attention to hygiene. If blood transfusion were harmful to health, how could they allow individuals to indulge in profit? Dr. Zhu's physical condition is as strong as ever, and he says, "I didn't feel weak or tired at all at the time. All large and small hospitals in the United States have a roster of blood donors." The claim that it is limited to the same clan and absolutely prohibits profit is based on what?

(3) Legal Observation (A) The issue of blood transfusion itself: in everything, one party benefits and the other suffers harm. Those who suffer harm enjoy legal protection. Those who harm others to benefit themselves are subject to legal sanctions to a certain extent. Currently, both blood recipients and blood donors benefit, so the issue of blood transfusion itself is legal, without a doubt. (B) When a doctor performs blood transfusion, the recipient benefits and the donor is unharmed. How can it be said that the rich are showing off their wealth and using money to lure the poor? They are simply using scientific knowledge and skills to save people! (C) Legal questions in the original text: those who publicly comment on people and affairs in writing should base every word and every sentence on solid evidence, especially when making suggestions to the Bar Association, requesting submissions to judicial administrative organs, and especially when it comes from the hand of a lawyer, and especially when it concerns human life! According to scientific principles, one should also speak with evidence.

From the Epidemic of Malignant Malaria to Disease Prevention 202

— Jiang Yeping

The seasons are changing one by one. It is said that today is changing from the "year of cholera" to the "year of malaria"! Of course, we do not believe in the fulfillment of prophecies, but the season of summer and autumn transition is a period of rampant disease. This is undeniable, with reality staring the public in the face. Past experiences confirm that the arrival of each summer is as terrifying as bringing disease and death.

Common Sense of Hygiene for Eye, Ear, Nose, and Throat Diseases 203

— Tang Renjin

(106) Speech and Voice Disorders Arising from Nasal Diseases

We have two types of breathing: nasal breathing and oral breathing. Therefore, the nasal cavity plays an important part in breathing. At the same time, it also has a close relationship with speech and sound, which is the so-called resonance effect of the nasal cavity. If there is a lesion in the nasal cavity, the resonance effect of the nasal cavity during vocalization will be abnormal. Its pitch will also clearly lose its normal state. This abnormal pitch is called nasal tone in medicine. Speech disorders due to nasal cavity lesions can be roughly divided into two categories.

(1) Obstructive Nasal Voice—Obstructive nasal voice is commonly seen in nasal colds (commonly known as head colds), hypertrophic rhinitis, adhesions in the nasal cavity, infiltration, ulceration, nasopharyngeal adhesions, and tumors. The degree varies, mostly depending on the location and severity of the nasal pain. In severe cases, the resonance effect of the nasal cavity can be completely abolished.

(2) Open Nasal Voice—Open nasal voice is more common in atrophy, destruction, and perforation of nasal tissues, perforation of the palate, defects of the soft palate, and infiltration. This is because when vocalizing, most of the exhaled air enters the nasal cavity.

(107) Nerve Disorders and Reflex Nerve Symptoms Arising from Nasal Diseases

Among the general nerve disorders arising from nasal diseases, the most common is headache. Headaches can be divided into two types: localized and widespread. Localized ones are limited to a local area, such as the root of the nose, the forehead, the temples, the top of the head, and the back of the head. Widespread ones radiate and affect the entire head. The intensity of the headache also varies. In mild cases, there is only a feeling of pressure. In severe cases, there is severe, stabbing pain. At this time, patients are mostly in great distress. Among nasal diseases, the most common and easiest to cause headaches are nasal obstruction and sinusitis. In addition, so-called nerve disorders include insomnia, early feelings of mental or physical fatigue, general fatigue, weakness, memory loss, and nasal attention deficit, etc. Among them, the so-called nasal attention deficit is more common in patients with high-degree nasal obstruction (mostly due to adenoid hypertrophy). They often cannot concentrate their attention and are often accompanied by memory loss and dizziness.

As for reflex nerve symptoms, they are generally characterized by asthma, nocturia, nervous tinnitus, cough, and genital disorders.

Recently, from newspapers and news, we have seen and heard of groups of precious lives dying from malignant malaria. This tragic news is constantly spreading, spreading quickly and widely. What a miserable and terrifying thing.

Everyone, who wants to send their own life to the god of death? But if you contract a disease and do not treat it properly, the illness will worsen, even to death. This is the inevitable result. Especially an infectious disease? It is very serious. Almost all counties in Jiangsu are experiencing this infectious disease. It's really scary!

Now we ask why malignant malaria is spreading like this? On the one hand, it is certainly related to the climate? But the biggest problem is the lack of prevention. Everyone knows that prevention is easier and more effective than treatment. Someone once said, "Modern medicine has progressed from therapeutic medicine to preventive medicine." But why is malignant malaria allowed to grow so severely? Although preventive medicine and preventive measures in China are still in their infancy, the public's lack of hygiene knowledge and the formality of attention from prevention agencies are also a major reason.

From this, we have learned a great lesson: health agencies should not only do some treatment work and formal publicity but should also pay close attention to the prevention of diseases for the public. For this type of malignant malaria, if we can pay attention to how to prevent it before it occurs or has not yet occurred, and if the health agencies publicize it to the public or enforce prevention, then I believe that at least the mortality rate will definitely not be so high!

Since what has happened in the past is already the past, then how should health agencies promote preventive medicine in the future? How to teach the public to pay attention to disease prevention? Now let's take an example: such as the provincial health office, its mission is of course to pay attention to public health and disease prevention, but in reality? How much effectiveness has it actually achieved? It is only the public in the provincial capital who enjoy its benefits! But what about the countryside? It is a question mark.

But in substance, comparing the number of deaths from malignant malaria this year in rural and urban areas, the number of deaths in rural areas is several times higher than in urban areas. Therefore, from this point, it is necessary to pay immediate attention to "rural hygiene"! This is not just an empty slogan; it is indeed a very important issue related to the health of the nation! Once an infectious disease occurs in the countryside, it is impossible to stop it. What a miserable thing! Here, we can provide some suggestions: we hope that the government will help each county organize "rural medical and health mobile teams" to take on the responsibility of teaching the public about disease prevention and at the same time train the public to know basic hygiene common sense. It is best to establish a voluntary health agency in each district office to be responsible for the health affairs of the district. Also, it is best to often give disguised speeches and use public gatherings to impart profound hygiene common sense.

Another point is why the public does not know how to pay attention to disease and hygiene? Of course, the public's superstitious beliefs are too deep! At the same time, there is no concrete understanding of scientific medicine. The biggest point is that the shackles of the economy bind them, and they can only use superstitious psychology to anesthetize patients, or hire quack doctors to temporarily comfort the sick. This is a very scary thing! Now, if we want to eliminate and sweep away harmful ideas and thoughts, the most important point is that we must educate the public!

We know that the reason for the failure of health agencies in the past is that they only paid attention to form and did not know how to enrich the content? In other words, this is the path that should be worked hard in the future! Everyone knows that the achievements of health agencies are the most difficult to fully demonstrate! We fully acknowledge this, but if the work of the health cause is diligent, we can say that the epidemic of infectious diseases and the reduction of the mortality rate can at least be reduced and lowered.

Now we summarize the above words, to make the public pay attention to disease prevention, the first requirement is to enrich their hygiene knowledge. The second is to pay immediate attention to "rural hygiene." The third is to set up more health agencies in the countryside. The fourth is to correct the public's misconceptions about scientific medicine. The fifth is to hope that health agencies start by enriching the content. Finally, we hope that all intellectuals will do their best to help publicize hygiene, and then it will be easy!

Finance: Gold Standard Continues to Prosper; Bulls Increase Positions, Bears Cover; Pure Gold Continues to Rise, Up Another 90 Cents 204

The gold market continued to strengthen yesterday due to the further rise in pure gold. However, there were also many sellers. It weakened slightly in the middle, but the bulls aggressively increased their positions and the bears also covered, resulting in further gains. In the early morning, overseas silver markets showed slight gains, and the London silver forward price rose between 0.6 and 1.0 percent. Exchange rates declined slightly, and London spot gold rose by one penny. The Central Bank's listed gold standard price was announced to be 1159.8 yuan, up 80 cents. In the over-the-counter forward market, prices opened at 52.50 yuan to 54 yuan, but there were no transactions. Fuxing and Yonglai sold and downstreamed. The opening was still high, but large players sold off, causing continued declines. However, large players took the opportunity to aggressively increase their positions. The HSBC's listed prices were the same for British and American currencies. The silver balancing tax was announced to be up by 1.5 cents, and gradually recovered. However, there was a lot of struggle in the middle due to many sellers. Later, the bears suddenly came in to cover, and the bulls took the opportunity to show their power, resulting in a stronger close in the afternoon. The market situation for the first half of the day is recorded below.

The opening price in the morning was 1153.1 yuan, up slightly by 20 cents from last Saturday. Fuxing, Yongyuan, and Maoyong sold off, retreating to 1152.6 yuan. Qiafeng, Yongcheng, Dajin, and Changyonglai bought in. HSBC's listed prices were the same for British and American currencies, and the silver balancing tax was announced to be up by 1.5 cents, recovering to 1153.1 yuan. Wanxing, Yuanmao, Yongheng, Yugan, Changxiang, Chunyuan, and Yongshanglai sold off, falling to 1153.1 yuan. Cheng, Qiafeng, Yongtong, Fusheng, and Yuanyong bought in one after another, gradually rising to 1153.9 yuan. The afternoon close was 1153.8 yuan.

The Central Bank's standard gold standard price was listed as 1159.8 yuan. According to the closing price, it was about 6 yuan higher. The account price for this month was 1151 yuan, and for last month it was 1154 yuan. The morning premium was 1151 yuan. Pure gold was increased by 6 yuan, to 1159.8 yuan. The price of Tianjian goods was increased by 12 yuan. The buying price of refined red gold was increased by 10 yuan, but there were no transactions. The selling price was increased by 13.5 yuan, and only 50 taels were sold by Tongliangheng to Hankou. In addition, the sellers have gradually become silent.

Over-the-counter trading was mediocre. In summary, Qiafeng, Yongcheng, Datong, Fuxing, Dayong, Qianchang, Xiangyi, Daheng, Changyongtong, Fengheng, Jingfu, etc. were on the buying side. Chunyuan, Yongfeng, Yuanmao, Yongheng, Yuanheng, Fuxing, Yongsheng, and Yuanyong, etc. were on the selling side. Yiren, Qianchang, and Xiang advanced first and then exited.

The market situation was stable in the first half of the day. The opening price in the morning was 1153.1 yuan, and the afternoon close was 1153.8 yuan. The highest price was 1153.9 yuan, and the lowest price was 1151.6 yuan, with a fluctuation of 1.3 yuan. As a result, it continued to rise by 90 cents from last Saturday. Only seven bars were left for this month, and there were 6797 counters for the November period. In total, there were 12 bulls. Medium transactions. A total of 1318 bars were traded.

Stable Foreign Exchange Market in the First Half of the Day - Active Settlement by Chinese Merchants 205

The foreign exchange market was relatively stable yesterday due to the first day of Qiushi, with only half a day of business. In the early morning, overseas telegrams reported that London's big bars rose by 25 points for both near and far terms. The silver market was uncertain. The Mondelli silver forward price rose by 0.6 to 0.50 percent. London spot gold rose by one penny. The British currency depreciated by 125 points against the US dollar, and rose by 21 pounds against the French franc, depreciating by 285 points against the pound. The US dollar was unchanged against the French franc. The Central Bank's listed prices were the same for British and American currencies. The Customs gold bill rose by only one cent. The standard gold standard price was listed at 155.8 yuan. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling price for British currency at 1 shilling and 2 pence flat and 563 toda. The US currency was 29.5625 yuan. Compared to last Saturday, the British and American currencies were flat. After the opening, banks were keen to sell far-term currencies. Japanese banks had more of a selling appetite. HSBC's listed prices were the same for British and American currencies, and there were many orders. Chinese merchants still had a strong selling appetite, and banks were still keen to buy. The silver balancing tax was announced to be up by 1.5 cents, showing struggles. Later, the process became stable due to foreign exchange trading. In the afternoon, the near-term selling price for British currency was 1 shilling and 2 pence and a half flat and 5625 toda. The US currency was 29.5625 yuan. Compared to last Saturday, the British and American currencies were flat for both near and far terms. Chinese merchants sold about 200,000 US dollars. The transactions for the first half of the day are recorded below.

The British currency opened in the morning with the near-term buying price at 1 shilling and 2 pence and a half flat and 5625 toda, with a profit settlement for February at 4375. HSBC bought November's first half of the month at 5325. Citibank sold spot goods to Datong at 5625 (setting British and American foreign exchange rates at 4.875). Magali settled November at 53125. Datong bought November at 5625. The closing selling price for spot goods was 1 shilling and 2 pence and 53125, half a penny for November, 46875 for November, and 4375 for January. The purchase price was slightly higher.

The US currency opened in the morning with the near-term selling price at 29.5625 yuan. Shanghai bought spot goods at 5625 and 625 toda. Zhenjin settled at the same price for the same month. Datong sold spot goods to Citibank at the same price (setting British and American foreign exchange rates at 487.75). Citibank and Datong bought half a yuan for January. Shanghai paid 5625 for December. Citibank bought at the same price for the same month. The closing buying price for spot goods was 29.5625 yuan, half a yuan for November, 4375 for December, and 375 for January. The purchase price was increased by 0.0625.

Securities: Public Bonds Remain in a Sideways Market 206

Yesterday, the market situation of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange turned tired. Although it generally remained sideways, large players such as No. 4 tended to sell, while the northern group took the opportunity to cover at low prices. In the end, it failed to break away from the principle of returning after a slight decline. Among the environmental factors, the most noteworthy was the multiple incidents in North China and the deteriorating situation in Suidong. However, before there is a significant development, the bond market will still be in a sideways state. The course of yesterday was dominated by selling pressure at the opening. It is said that the selling of No. 4 had a significant background. Sellers on the market were seen to be enthusiastic. Bonds such as No. 8, 16, 32, and 47 were sold off. The market price unanimously trended weaker. Except for the B type for this month, which was still good by 5 cents, the rest were uniformly down by 5 cents to 1 jiao. The B type for this month was down by as much as 3 jiao, which was caused by the selling of No. 4. After the opening in the afternoon, trading was sparse, with swap transactions accounting for the majority. Market prices were previously down by 1-2 jiao, and later gradually turned firmer. At the close, retail investors covered their short positions, and unanimously turned slightly firmer by 5 cents to 1 jiao and a half. As a result of the market price, the B type for this month was good by 5 cents, and the rest uniformly recovered by 5 cents to 1 jiao to 2 jiao and a half. The total transaction volume was 4.3 million yuan. The comparison of the rise and fall results is listed on the left. (Unit: Yuan, transaction units: hundreds of yuan)

Cotton Yarn, Yarn Prices Get New Boost 208

The yarn market was tired in the morning and rose in the afternoon, but now yarn sales have turned dull. Customers are slow to purchase. The prices for November delivery yarn are now equal to the spot yarn prices. There are still many people who sell when prices rise. It is said that after the New Year, some yarn factories may have labor strikes, with workers demanding wage increases. At the same time, Osaka Sampin (Three Products) yarn has recently seen a speculative surge of six yuan, boosting morale, and market prices have returned to a favorable state.

Yarn Prices Rebound After the New Year

The pre-market opening for futures yarn showed tight conditions for this month's delivery due to the scarcity of spot yarn. Prices continued to rise. Further-dated contracts were relatively stable. After the second session, news of sluggish yarn sales and easing raw cotton prices caused the market to decline. The result of the futures trading was unchanged for this month's delivery, while further-dated contracts fell by four, five, and seven jiao (cents) compared to the previous day's closing price.

In the afternoon session, the market situation for this month's delivery tightened again. Rumors of labor strikes in factories boosted morale. At the same time, Osaka Sampin yarn market surged sharply, further hardening the market. The result of the futures trading was that prices for all months rose by one yuan, three, five, seven, and eight jiao compared to the morning closing price.

Purchases included: Yuda 1,600 bales, Hengyi 1,600 bales, Quxing 1,900 bales, Mingde 1,800 bales, Hexing 6,500 bales, Shenchang 1,300 bales, Xingchang 1,750 bales, Renfeng 1,250 bales, Changfeng 3,450 bales, Runkang 2,800 bales, Jinkang 1,500 bales, Yicheng 1,500 bales.

Sales included: Yiji 1,350 bales, Yuda 1,250 bales, Jinchang 8,700 bales, Shenji 4,200 bales, Dachangcheng 1,450 bales, Taichang 1,100 bales, Yichang 1,800 bales, Dachang 1,700 bales, Qingfeng 1,700 bales, Xincheng 1,050 bales.

Continuous Arrivals, Cotton Pre-Market Selling Pressure Intense, Afternoon Profit-Taking Rebound Tightens Market 209

The cotton market initially fell and then rebounded. Initially, abundant arrivals from various routes and increased inventory levels dampened morale. Subsequently, a favorable yarn market and a rebound in the Osaka Sampin cotton market, coupled with expectations of a slight increase in US cotton estimates for tomorrow, led to rising market prices and a sharp rise in buying interest, rebounding by 2.3 jiao. However, this month's contract broke through the 40-yuan mark.

(This Month's Contract Re-enters the 40-Yuan Level)

The pre-market opening for cotton futures was characterized by weak sentiment due to hopes of an increase in US cotton estimates, intensifying selling pressure. Large traders poured in to sell, flooding the market, and prices steadily declined. The near-term contract broke through the 40-yuan mark. The result of the futures trading was that prices for all months fell by four, five, six, and seven jiao compared to the previous day's closing price.

The afternoon session opened with a rebound in Osaka Sampin cotton, leading profit-takers to cover their positions, tightening the market and boosting momentum. As a result, prices for all months rose by two and three jiao compared to the morning closing price.

Sales included: Heyu 22,800 dan (a unit of weight), Yuda 16,100 dan, Huamao 1,800 dan, Renfeng 2,100 dan, Wuyi 3,400 dan, Dachangcheng 2,600 dan, Dachang 3,200 dan, Changhe 11,400 dan, Senkang 3,500 dan, Runkang 3,600 dan, Yuanxingchang 2,500 dan, Hengyi 3,700 dan, Zhenda 8,100 dan, Jinchang 4,000 dan, Qingfeng 12,800 dan, Shenchang 2,800 dan, Shenji 2,400 dan, Taichang 5,000 dan, Yichang 4,500 dan, Changfeng 5,000 dan, Shengyuan 4,300 dan, Fukang 3,000 dan, Xinchang 3,000 dan.

Settlement Prices for April Delivery Yarn and Cotton 210

Following the dispute over the April standard yarn and cotton contracts at the Chinese Merchants' Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange, the May contract was removed on the 6th. It was found that 18,650 bales of cotton yarn and 21,400 dan of cotton were traded. The directors of the exchange went to Beijing to petition, and have already returned to Shanghai. According to the market, the cotton yarn price (closing price on the 5th) was 214.6 yuan. The long side compensated 1 yuan, and the short side compensated 5 jiao. The cotton price (closing price on the 5th) was 41.55 yuan. The long side compensated 2.5 jiao, and the short side compensated 5 jiao. It is said that one party is still dissatisfied with this arrangement, and the final outcome remains to be seen.

The price for the near month was 66.45 yuan, and the price for the far month was 66.95 yuan.

Piece Goods: Chinese and Foreign Yarn Prices Increase, Sales of Chinese and Japanese Factory Cloth are Particularly Smooth – Selling Prices for Various Goods Gradually Increase – 213

Yesterday, the cloth market saw a sharp rise in the price of Sanpin yarn, and the situation of both futures and spot yarn was firm. Japanese trading houses and factories raised the prices of white goods, fine cloth, fine twill, and 84 cloth by 1-2 jiao per piece, which improved morale, and customer sales gradually started to pick up. Dyeing factories on this street replenished their stocks of dyed fine cloth and fine twill for both spot and futures delivery by more than 500 bales. Dealers along the Yangtze River, such as Changsha, Changde, Hankou, and Anqing, increased their purchases, and transactions were mainly for fine twill, fine cloth, printed flannelette, serge, drill, and white flannelette from Chinese and foreign factories. Among them, Hankou merchants purchased the largest amount of fine cloth and fine twill, exceeding 800 pieces, with brisk actual sales. The cloth sales market also turned prosperous. Yesterday, merchants from this street and the Yangtze River purchased 400-500 bales, and spot goods are gradually becoming scarce. The inventory of patterned goods and flannelette on the market is also low, and sales are particularly smooth. Selling prices have generally not changed, but the selling prices of colored cloth and colored twill from various factories have gradually increased due to the rising price of grey cloth.

Woolen Fabrics are Surprisingly Firm 214

Yesterday, the woolen fabric market saw active trading, and standard prices were very firm. Prices generally opened higher in the morning and closed even higher in the evening. Street runners and brokers were very busy, and goods at the original price were often out of stock. The strength of the market was truly rare in the past three to five years. Therefore, most woolen fabric brokers with some reputation or financial resources are absorbing goods or paying deposits in advance, using skillful tactics to make profits. On the other hand, those who work hard to run around find it difficult to profit, because the market is short of goods, and sellers mostly want cash, and even refuse to cut small samples.

Grains: Rumors of Australian Wheat Price Approaching, Futures Flour Market Sentiment Turns Soft, Yesterday's Results Decline by Two or Three Points, Security Deposit Returns to Old Rules Today, 250 Yuan Per 1,000 Bags 215

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the prices of all months were initially stable and then fell sharply. When the prices of foreign wheat were quoted, Chicago was slightly better by nearly a jiao, and Canada was lower by four or five fen. When the prices were opened, sentiment was still stable, and this month's to January's contracts were slightly better by about one fen. When February's price was opened, sentiment gradually softened. Because the market widely rumored that there was news about Australian wheat, and the current asking price was 8.76 yuan (about 8-9 jiao different from the standard here), this reason caused sentiment to soften. The previous continuous rise, fearing that wheat production would not be sufficient for application, is now difficult to sustain. When the afternoon session opened, sentiment was even softer, falling by nearly a fen compared to the morning session. Because the environment is gradually changing, speculation from outside the industry will inevitably decrease, so subsequent steps will gradually become flat. The exchange market is also stable. It is now set that from the 10th, the security deposit will return to normal, which is 250 yuan per 1,000 bags.
