Snippets 222

— (Tai Xuan)

"It takes one year to kill a tree, ten years to grow a tree, and a hundred years to cultivate a person." Therefore, those who govern the country must struggle through the difficult and arduous path of being as cautious as approaching a deep abyss and treading on thin ice in order to carve out a path to life. This great path built with blood and sweat requires sacrificing millions of heads as a cornerstone-laying ceremony before there is a hope of completion.

Inferring from the differences in years between killing a tree, growing a tree, and cultivating a person, if we want to place the country on the security of a solid rock, then we must at least consider a century-long plan. From the Opium War to the present, there have been nearly a hundred years. The invasions and humiliations suffered during these hundred years are truly unimaginable. Several million square li of the country and tens of millions of compatriots are reaching out to us for help in the darkness. This is the great responsibility we must shoulder, and this is the responsibility we must keep in mind every day and never forget.

In order to complete the century-long plan of establishing the country, the first requirement is that we must be self-reliant. If anyone wants to infringe upon our self-existence and self-reliance or hinder our self-existence and self-reliance, then we can only fight them to the death, because only by fighting to the death can we find a way out of desperation. Now we have reached the final juncture mentioned above, and it remains to be seen whether the aggressors can pull back from the brink. In order to ensure the great plan of the country's self-existence and self-reliance, 450 million compatriots have already stood on the same front.

Friendship 223

— Zhu Ying

What exactly does friendship look like? How exactly should it be maintained? I don't know.

When I stepped out of the school gate, I used to see more than five classmates. Not only did we write to each other three times a month, but we also had a considerable amount of friendship. Day and night, we would do certain things together. What's more, they thought highly of me, and they would never forget to give me a red card or a white card for weddings, funerals, and celebrations. And I always went to congratulate or mourn within the possible range. Then, I got married myself and sent out red cards, but three of them didn't respond. A year later, my late father passed away, and I sent out white cards, and then there were four more. They didn't offer condolences to me, and they stopped communicating. A year later, I lost my job, so I wrote letters to the classmates who still had friendships, asking them to pay attention to introducing me to jobs. Unexpectedly, after this letter was sent out, only four of them replied, promising to pay attention to it. The rest simply had no news at all. To this day, everyone doesn't know where they have gone. One of those four who remained, because I had moved a sum of money from him once, was afraid to meet me and didn't communicate with me either. Although I returned both loans with interest as scheduled, without any arrears, he was unhappy to associate with me because of this, which was also an unavoidable matter. There was also one who had asked me to borrow ten yuan, and then asked me to borrow five yuan. From then on, he hid from me from afar when he saw me on the street. At the end of the year, the New Year's card didn't come either. The New Year's card I sent wasn't returned by the post office either. It turned out that he had moved to who knows where. The third one asked me to borrow a very considerable amount of money, but I couldn't help because I didn't have the ability, and I replied refusing him. As a result, I received his letter of severance filled with complaints and resentment. Now, the only classmate who still maintains friendship is only one left, but I don't know if this one will also abandon me one day.

Four years ago, I used to date a girlfriend. This girlfriend's temperament was gentle, her conversation was refined, and her knowledge was above the waterline. Because she was similar to my habits, the two of us developed a very close friendship. I am a married man, and I am driven by the spurs of life, absolutely not possessing any ambitions. Therefore, my attitude towards that girlfriend absolutely did not cross the boundaries of friendship. Although we wrote to each other two or three times a month and talked on the phone four or five times, and even went to see plays and travel to the suburbs together, we absolutely did not involve any private affairs. After interacting for three years, she subtly revealed her intention to be my life partner, and I hastily and righteously refused. Then, she found a partner and held a wedding. When she got married, I also went to congratulate her very sincerely. Unexpectedly, after she got married, she abandoned her original friendship. Both times I went to visit, she said she wasn't home. Once, she was walking on the street with her husband, and when she saw me at a glance, she lowered her head and pretended not to see me. Recently, I wrote a letter of greeting, and a week later, I received her reply, saying that in order to avoid suspicion, she asked me not to write any more letters in the future. I then knew that what we originally had wasn't friendship at all.

Review of the National Cartoon Exhibition 224

— Liu Shi

The "National Cartoon Exhibition," which everyone had been looking forward to for a long time, finally opened on the 4th of this month at Daxin. According to the person in charge, this exhibition was prepared in a hurry, so although the name written on it was "National," in reality "national writers" were not able to be gathered in one fell swoop.

However, in terms of quantity, it is already very considerable. As for the quality, it seems to be somewhat lacking.

The history of comics in China is very short, but it has been able to forge ahead to this point in a very short period of time and obtain such excellent fruits. This is already no easy task. Originally, we shouldn't have any more harsh demands. However, the mission of comics is to stand on the front lines of the era like a suicide squad and charge! Kill! Moreover, the current world situation and the current Chinese society can no longer tolerate leisurely, intoxicated, amorous, carnal, or even meaningless comic books. Instead, it needs to strike at the central ideology, contain profound meaning, express the dynamics of world thought, expose the darkness of current society, and bear the inescapable responsibility of holding the authority of humor and satire that can influence social thought, improve social customs, and build the will of young people.

For example, the few monochrome comics signed by Chen Yifan in the exhibition show that the author's skills and thoughts are quite cultivated. There are no bright colors on the surface of his books, but they can attract the audience. It makes people want to see it again after seeing it, and it really has the effect of so-called never getting tired of watching. Of course, some people say that comics do not need to emphasize skills, as long as they have thoughts. That's right, if you can be like Mr. Chen, with both skills and thoughts, wouldn't it be more perfect? Furthermore, such as the few comic portraits of Guangyu, Zhengyu, and Qianyu; of course, you can't read anything meaningful from portraits, but they all have pure and wonderful skills, so they also give the audience a deep impression. There are also several "artistic" comic books signed by Hua Lu, whose colors, lines, and composition are extremely fresh, "purely artistic", and "genius." But, it's a pity that "thought" is not very sound.

There are many other good works that cannot be introduced one by one. In short, like the ones mentioned above, their common shortcoming is that they pay too much attention to fun. In other words, there are too few progressive things, and there are too many boring things. Regarding this, we are very interested in expecting, expecting them to give us a satisfactory answer at the second National Cartoon Exhibition.

Goldfish Ramblings 225

— Wu Jiren

Since the beginning of autumn, a strange drought has persisted, leaving pools and ponds parched for days. The water fleas, the goldfish's only food source, have disappeared as a result. Recently, goldfish breeders in Shanghai have all switched to feeding porridge grains. As for those who rely on fish for a living, they usually venture out in all directions to catch them, but it is often difficult to even get one-tenth of what they need. Therefore, this year, "Fat Heads" rarely exceed two inches in length. If a breeder has one or two hundred tanks, the fish's bodies become thin and their spines weakened. I have heard that in some gardens, the well water has dried up, and there is no way to carry water. The small fish are left to wither, and the fish servants look up to the sky and sigh, wondering what to do.

Recently, my mother-in-law became ill with asthma and was sent home. During my leisure time, I inquired with fellow fish breeders in the Suzhou area. They said that they have not been able to provide live food for over a month and are using porridge to nurture them. They all believe that the fish market will be a poor one this year. The impact of the drought on aquatic products is indeed significant.

Since I designed and customized "fish cups" for Guanshengyuan this spring, several hundred dozen have sold like hotcakes. From this, I know that there are many more fish lovers in Shanghai. I once commissioned a kiln to produce a kind of "Qingsha fish tank," imitating the small size of Tianjin tanks but with a wider opening, allowing for ample sunlight. I named it "Tan." The first batch of twenty were quickly taken by friends. I have ordered dozens more. Gentlemen such as Chen Renhe, Zhou Jianyun, and Xi Yushu have all placed several in their residences. Using "Tan" to raise goldfish has several advantages, such as producing plump bodies, short bodies, prominent head and horns, large and strong tails that spread out in four directions, easy greening of the water, and hearty appetites. This spring, I chose fish with correct body shapes to raise in the "Tan," placing twenty fish in each "Tan" and giving them plenty of live food every day. I added water every night. After ten days, the fish had grown larger by one inch (originally half an inch, now one inch). I then scooped out ten fish and raised them separately, feeding them in the same way. In less than half a month, they doubled in size again. If you want them to grow even bigger, you can move them to a cement pond, providing them with ample food and constantly flushing the water. After a summer, this year's goldfish will have grown to four inches. It is said that fish in ponds will inevitably grow long, but after dozens of days of regulation in the "Tan," you can be sure that they will not have to worry about losing their shape. Bao Tianxiao also raises several tanks of famous pearl goldfish in his Shanghai residence. Among them, there are only two or three pairs of "water bubble eye" fish with inverted heads, which have been raised in the "Tan" and are rarely seen elsewhere.

I met with Mr. Fan Yunshu, Director of Suzhou Park, who told me that the annual goldfish and chrysanthemum exhibition has been scheduled in cooperation with the Suzhou Agricultural School and will be held around November 10th in the park. They are seeking submissions of famous goldfish and chrysanthemums from public and private collections in the Wuzhong area. The grand occasion at that time can be predicted, and I will write more after viewing it.

The Salaried Class 226

— Manzi

The average salaried person experiences two kinds of suffering: first, the lack of financial support after retirement; and second, the lack of security in the event of disability during their working life. Obviously, there are many factories, schools, and businesses that have group insurance, pensions, and bereavement benefits, but these are in the minority. For the vast majority, just receiving their monthly salary on time, without any delay, is already a cause for great joy.

"Night Meeting" depicts a chemist who is loyal to his factory. Fearing that an explosion of chemicals would destroy the entire factory, he risked his life to protect it, resulting in injuries to his eyes. The factory, seeing that he was disabled, gave him some medical expenses and a small sum of money, terminating his employment. A happy family that depended entirely on his salary was plunged into a tragic situation. Observers lamented: In this day and age, can those who live on salaries really have no security? I think that anyone who hears this will feel a pang of bitterness in their heart.

On the other hand, it depicts a woman without higher education who, in order to secure her family's livelihood, does not hesitate to sacrifice her appearance and work as a general hostess in a nightclub. The meager salary she earns is barely enough to make ends meet, and she is unable to meet her needs. As a result, she is forced to kill. Aren't female hostesses a very common and growing part of the salaried class in today's society? When they put on smiling faces to greet customers, the customers only focus on their appearance. Who can imagine that behind them, there is a group of starving family members? Who can see the immeasurable pain in their hearts?

Therefore, "Night Meeting" is nothing less than a cry for the salaried class, a demand for a solution for the salaried class. Its significance is very serious. I hope that the audience will not be dazzled by the magnificent scenes, intoxicated by the bright lights and alcohol, or fascinated by the charming smiles, because this film resonates with millions of salaried people.

Mysterious ×× 227

— Zi

×× is mysterious. In the minds of writers, it represents something incomprehensible. In the minds of mathematicians, it represents a mathematical symbol. On the political stage, some people use it to represent a certain Eastern country. But I think no one will mistake its temporary meaning? Ah! ×× is so mysterious.

Swapping the Nest: A Tale of Luan and Phoenix 228

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Vows of Allegiance over a Cup of Water, Whispers of Sorrow under a Green Lamp; Agreements Sealed with Golden Rings, Messages of Love Borne by Red Beans

The subject I have the least confidence in is geometry. Randomly flipping through the book, I find every question vague. I must take advantage of this cool weather to memorize more theorems. So, I calmed my mind and picked up a geometry book. In the past, when I calmed down to read, I could always absorb some of it into my brain. But today, the more I read, the more confused I become. So, I put the book aside for a while and picked up a magazine from the bookshelf. Flipping through it, I found several small poems full of emotion. After reading them, I found them quite enjoyable to recite. After reciting them, and then carefully savoring them, I felt my heart fill with flavor. Unconsciously, I spent an hour reading the magazine. Then I remembered that it was time to review my lessons. How could I waste my time so casually? So, I moved the magazine aside and picked up my lessons again. I repeated these actions, flipping back and forth, unable to control myself. Soon, it was after dinner, and the room was lit. I was lost in thought under the light, wondering how to spend this lonely evening. Just then, I heard Youmei's voice downstairs. She said, "You have already seen Mrs. Jiang off. You brought me here and went back, so you have finished your errand. Why are you still following me?" Then I heard a woman answer, "I want to go upstairs to pay my respects to Miss Jiang." Menglan greeted them at the door of her room, leaning against the railing, and smiled down, "You are a woman of your word. You said you would come, and you came." As she spoke, she noticed a maid behind her. She smiled and said, "Mei, do you still need someone to tie you up to bring you here?" The maid stepped forward and raised her head to the upper floor, saying, "Miss Jiang, our mistress said that our young lady is bothering you here. Please don't be too polite." Menglan laughed at her, "Alright, hand her over to me. You can go back." The maid smiled and really left. Youmei came upstairs, first shook Menglan's hand and whispered, "Look, the children of every family are worried about and controlled by their parents like this!" Menglan nodded. Then the two of them sat together at the table, separated by a white porcelain kerosene lamp, looking at each other. Little Ju'er brought chrysanthemum tea and placed four plates of dried snacks on the table. Youmei laughed, "It's like you knew I was coming and prepared these things for guests." Menglan laughed, "Because your credibility in front of me is very good, I knew you would come. I didn't need to expect you." Little Ju, go downstairs. Little Ju stood firmly by the door, staring blankly at the two of them, then laughed, "Miss doesn't call me, I won't come up, okay?" (96)

World News

The Inside Story of Japan's Bid for the Next World Games Location 229

— Yifa

The 12th World Games has been decided to be held in Tokyo, Japan, and the citizens of Tokyo are all dreaming of the prosperous scene during the Games. This is the first time that the World Games will be held in the East. The reason why it was decided to be held in the East is not because Japan's sporting achievements are so excellent, but because the attention of Europe and the United States is focused on the East due to international relations. On the one hand, Japan has also worked very hard on the activities to determine the location of the World Games. Our country, which is rapidly building new infrastructure, may one day have the World Games decided to be held at the foot of Zijin Mountain in Nanjing. Do not let Japan have all the glory.

Japan's activities to bid for the World Games location started as early as seven years ago. The President of the International Association of Athletics Federations, Mr. Edström, traveled to Japan. He is Swedish. At the welcome banquet of the Japan Student Athletic Association, a student suddenly spoke and asked, "Will the World Games be held in Tokyo?" "Nothing is impossible. As long as you submit a request to the committee and add procedural intervention," the President said. It happened to coincide with the 2,600th anniversary of the founding of the country. Therefore, this (Tokyo World Games bid) was passed in the city council. In addition to sending councilors to Europe to campaign, they also asked ambassadors from various countries for assistance.

During the Lausanne Conference, Japan sent five officials to investigate and communicate with the World Games Committee, formally submitting a request. They also printed many photo propaganda materials and sent them to the committee members of various countries. Last year, the World Games Committee met in Via Sello. At that time, Tokyo was also determined to be one of the candidate cities. There were more than ten cities that requested, with Tokyo and Rome being the most promising. Later, Italy voluntarily withdrew due to financial difficulties, but a new force from Finland was added. On Finland's propaganda materials, each statistical country book was based on the proportion of population income to the World Games score. Finland's highest was 3.7, and Japan was at the bottom, with only 0.5. It was said that "Japan's sports world has not yet been enlightened, and Tokyo is of course not qualified to hold the Games." The Japanese were extremely embarrassed when they saw it.

This year, the President of the World Games, Mr. Berg, was brought to Japan by the Japanese for a trip. The World Games Preparation Committee was openly organized by Texas and made every effort to win him over. Ten days before the vote, Tokyo and London had equal hopes. Its success was entirely due to the help of Mr. Berg. When Mr. Berg was in Japan, he had already seen the design drawings of the next Games venue prepared by Japan and thought that Japan was actively preparing. Who knew that these were specially made for Mr. Berg to watch. Now that the World Games have been decided in Japan, there is still no definite construction plan. The newspaper propaganda is just a blank sheet of paper.

Japan's expenses for bidding for the World Games location from 1932 to the present have cost 480,000 yuan. This time, inviting Mr. Berg to Japan cost 45,000 yuan in hospitality expenses. The publicity fees, communication fees, and entertainment fees in Berlin were about 60,000 yuan. From this point of view, it is so difficult to compete for a World Games location.

Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao

Talk

Puppet Troops Attack Northern Suiyuan 230

— I

According to yesterday's newspaper, the puppet troops under Zhang Haipeng invaded westward from Chengde, and 3,000 troops under Bao Yueqing were also transferred from Western Rehe. It is said that the various units are using Bailingmiao as a gathering center and then advancing towards Eastern and Northern Suiyuan. Furthermore, the puppet cavalry in Northern Chahar has already begun to attack Northern Suiyuan. It is reported that Fu Zuoyi convened a military conference in Guihua to make proper arrangements for the defense of Northern Suiyuan. They are currently in a stalemate. Their westward policy and desire to invade Eastern and Northern Suiyuan have been long-standing. Therefore, the urgent news from Suiyuan has been flying in like snowflakes in recent days. However, today the situation is even more tense. The so-called two armies in a stalemate is just like in old novels, when the two armies face each other, and a general comes out from the opening of the flag gate. This is such an urgent situation.

The outcome of this war is something to be seen in the next episode. But we always know the importance of Chahar and Suiyuan. Chahar and Suiyuan are areas with abundant natural resources and also serve as a barrier for the northern provinces. Because the current so-called Great Wall can no longer serve as a dangerous fortress, if Chahar and Suiyuan are lost, the so-called Great Wall will be shared with the enemy. I am not clear about the current situation in Chahar. Now I only see the urgent news from Suiyuan. If Suiyuan cannot be defended, then the provinces within the Great Wall will be in danger. We must not despise Suiyuan just because it is far outside the Great Wall.

According to the Da Mei Evening News, the unofficial preparatory negotiations between China and Japan in recent days are no less important than the official diplomatic negotiations. Gao Zongwu and Suma will hold another unofficial meeting tomorrow to seek compromises on the points where China and Japan cannot agree. Originally, most things in the world can be discussed. But suppose A and B are discussing something, and A says, "Please open your heart and give it to me," or "Please dissect a certain part of your body and give it to me." No matter how accommodating B is, he will never allow it, right? Pingjin is our heart, and Chahar and Suiyuan are our limbs. How can we give even an inch of land or a iota of sovereignty to others? This is something that cannot be agreed to by any method of intimidation or deception.

Therefore, I dare to believe that no matter how long the Sino-Japanese negotiations last, it will be difficult to achieve a satisfactory result. I am not hoping for a breakdown in the negotiations between the two sides, because based on factual observation, there is really no possibility of compromise between the two sides. Moreover, while one side is negotiating, the news of the puppet troops attacking westward and advancing towards Northern Suiyuan has been repeatedly reported. This kind of action completely indicates a desire not to resolve the issue peacefully. We believe that the Suiyuan authorities must have a satisfactory response, and the central authorities must also have a way to deal with the aftermath properly and not regard it as an ordinary foreign disaster. Therefore, if we want to see whether the Sino-Japanese negotiations can be resolved, we must first see whether the actions of the puppet troops in Suiyuan can be stopped.

A Married Couple 231

— Linna

Almost every day, at a certain fixed time, we can see him, a tobacco seller carrying a large leather suitcase and holding ten or so new tobacco pipes, silently striding into the store, putting the leather suitcase of tobacco on the glass counter, reaching out to wipe the sweat from his face; then he asks in a low voice: "Boss, do you want tobacco today?"

We immediately go to check the tobacco box, and then reply: "Half a catty - that's it: don't need anymore, that's all."

And he will silently carry his suitcase, walk out of the store, and go to the next one, walking away.

This guy is from Yongchun. I've known him for almost a year or more. He is very quiet, doesn't joke, and doesn't say extra words. On his tall body, apart from that set of sky-blue linen short clothes and pants, a bamboo pointed hat on his head, a bamboo hat removed which reveals a black braid coiled up like cow dung, bare feet with a pair of multi-eared straw sandals, we haven't seen him dress up in any other way. Even during the fervent Christmas, New Year's, he is like this, the only difference is sitting at home smoking a dry pipe!

"He is a monster!" Almost all the merchants who have dealings with him think this way. Imperceptibly, he has gradually attracted attention, and is regarded as a symbol of mystery.

One day, we were made uneasy by a strange piece of news, the news came from a Cantonese peddler. He reported to everyone that this Yongchun man already has a beautiful Tangshan wife in Manila, who was brought there by one of his cousins ​​last year, and he also runs a tobacco shop in Insular, managed by this woman. After speaking, he blinked his small eyes, and waved his hands, depicting. This not only made us begin to pay great attention to this Yongchun man, but also felt very interested: so, whenever he came to our store to peddle tobacco, we often asked with a smile:

"Yongchun man, I heard that here, you have a Tangshan wife?"

He blushed, and silently stared at everyone, as if saying: Why do you want to mind these idle affairs?

"Very beautiful, everyone says so."

He didn't answer a word, as if he had been insulted, picked up his suitcase, and silently strode out of the store again. However, when he came the next day, he would be like nothing had happened: "Boss, do you want tobacco today?"

One day, in the afternoon, I was sent out by the store to collect debts, and I met him by the Male Bridge. He had sold all his goods and was just about to go home. I waved to him from afar, and quickly took a few steps to catch up with him. "Sold out?" I asked in a low voice. "Going home!" he said without even looking at me, his face still low to the ground.

"Where is your home?"

"Insular, there's the shop I opened." I thought to myself: "Why not go with him to see?" So I changed my tone and asked: "Can I go with you?"

He raised his head for the first time, looking at me, as if still a little uneasy. Seeing that I had no malice, or the appearance of mocking him, he silently nodded and said quietly: "I am very happy!"

We didn't say anything, quietly went around the city park, turned the corner of the Poler waste ground, and walked along a dark little street.

This street is almost built outside the city, desolate and lonely. On both sides of the street are squeezed dozens of old zinc houses, some are used as residences, some are used as small shops, in Manila, this is designated as a residential area for the poor, the types and population are equally numerous and complex, there are Spaniards, there are Japanese, there are Chinese and local aborigines.

Next to a wooden bridge that crosses a turbid mud river, there is a small zinc house, and there is a horizontal signboard on the roof that extends over half the street, with five large Chinese characters written in crooked characters "Zhengxing Tobacco Shop", below is a line of English, also written in the same clumsy style, we were on the slope on this side of the bridge, he pointed to the sign from afar, telling me:

"See? That's the tobacco shop I opened."

We slowly walked towards the slope under the bridge, to the point where we could see the street on the other side of the bridge. Suddenly I was absorbed by a chaotic scene, there, there was a group of children standing outside the tobacco shop, raising their two small arms, and throwing the sand and soil in their hands into the shop. From the shop came a burst of scolding. A young woman, with a high bun tied on her head, wearing a set of black jackets on the upper and lower body, holding a dry tobacco pipe in her hand, ran out in great strides, the children were frightened and scattered, clapping their hands and shouting:

"Look, the little-footed China woman..."

This made me think of it, and began to pay attention, yes, she is little-footed, wearing a pair of embroidered shoes, but, she acts as self-assured as an ordinary person, waving the weapon in her hand, laughing and chasing away those little devils.

When we entered the shop, the Yongchun man put down the suitcase on his back, those little devils had all hidden in a fence, she also turned back as if nothing had happened, and laughed without a bit of girlishness:

"These little devils, shout every day: look at the little feet of Chinese women! When they really run out to show them, they all run away one by one..."

Her bold attitude deeply shocked me.

Grandmother's House 232

— Bozi

Today, I have come to the countryside again.

I wish there were a few beautiful moonlit nights, so that Dengdi and I could go to the threshing ground to listen to the sounds of frogs, the sounds of snake birds, the sounds of rushing water on the threshing ground. So that Dengdi and I could go to the threshing ground to see the moon, the village in the moonlight, the huge field in front of the village, and see the small wind blowing ripples across the water seedlings in the field. I walked along, making these dreams. My wife slowly lagged behind, with the nanny: she seemed tired, always staggering like that. We walked past the ping, we went around the bay, we passed through one village after another.

The road drew familiar curves in my memory, and the undulating, distant mountains also seemed to have been drawn by my hand.

A light breeze was on our hair, on our clothes, and on the waves over there, a light breeze, in gusts. So, my childhood memories slowly came: I stepped into childhood -

Everything is the same, even though it is a very, very small reed. We, bare-shouldered and back, often walked this road, clothes tied on the top of the head, as a shield from the sun.

"Children, aren't you afraid of drowning?"

One day, Uncle Milong met us, that hunchbacked old man who disgusts us, he knew that we were going to Jiyu Pool to swim and play.

"We won't!"

My companions and I answered him in unison; but that time, Dengdi was indeed in a bit of danger, at that time, Dengdi was not qualified to play in the water with us!

As soon as we finished washing, we started to pick a reed on this road, pulling out the thin reed stems one by one from a leaf, and taking them back to use as arrows for tomorrow's battle. This road was our paradise in the past! Thinking about it, it's like yesterday, can be counted vividly.

But now it is September after the private harvest, Dengdi's wedding date, I heard, is at the end of this October, in the blink of an eye, this child is almost an adult!

I was a little dazed.

I stared at the stream over there, a stream with rippled water blown by the wind - a shallow stream. I slowed down.

Turning a wooden bridge, I saw the oil mill hiding under the maple tree, from the oil mill to Wanjiana, only as far as a pipe of tobacco, I still remember when I was a child, I often played chess under the roots of this tree with kids of the same age, if something went wrong, we would start cursing each other, scolding a bunch of wild words, and disbanding. Now, where have those guys who liked to curse gone? They have probably all grown up, right? Not enough to have a decisive argument for a game of "Nine Sons", right? So I asked my wife:

"Do you still remember Man Niu?"

"He is our tenant farmer."

"Do you still remember Hei Gou?"

"He is our tenant farmer."

"Wangsheng?"

"Also."

Tenant farmers? I thought. I almost didn't believe my wife, how could things be so different in just seven or eight years, I was a little suspicious.

Thinking of the past, I told my wife the story of washing, the story of picking reeds to use as arrows, and the story of always quarreling while playing chess. Tell my wife? I was worried that my wife wouldn't understand.

My wife followed behind, and I could hear a bit of panting.

We were on the road - in front of the oil mill, under our feet was a small stream, there were women washing clothes by the stream, and when they found us, they giggled and laughed from afar.

That is my grandmother's house, emerging above the bamboo forest, that lonely roof.

I turned my head and said to my wife: "We are almost at grandma's house!"

For the first time, I learned to say like my son: my wife just smiled, shyly.

Shepherdess 233

— Hao Lin

Whenever someone mentions the shepherdess Li Sha, people can't help but sigh.

It really is a tragic destiny. It was only two years ago that Li Sha was a happy person, and she was the most beautiful of all the girls, with a strong body and lively youth. What made her most proud was her Gilbert Lai (Note 1). Which girl in the mountains didn't envy her such happiness?

Gilbert Lai was Li Sha's lover. He wasn't actually called by that name; it was a nickname given by her female companions. His real name was Sabuqi.

During a certain festival's competition, they were both selected to join the singing team. During the competition, the clear and resounding songs of these two people were captivating to the attendees, and it's likely that even Ayi (Note 2) was mesmerized. Therefore, Sabuqi from the male group and Li Sha from the female group were instantly known to everyone. They also met at this time.

Sabuqi lived on the mountain across the river, but this didn't hinder them much. Every day, he would paddle a small canoe across to this side. Li Sha, standing on the high cliff, would excitedly run down to greet him as soon as she saw Sabuqi's canoe paddling to the shore, neglecting her own sheep, only caring about being with him.

In the depths of the forest, there were often traces of this pair. People who passed by them would always hear the innocent laughter of the two, as happy as little birds in the trees, seemingly unaware of what sorrow was in their lives. Sometimes, when they were happy, they would sing at the top of their lungs, their songs melodious, even the thickets in the forest listening in silence. I remember one late night when the bright moon shone high in the sky, people gathered by the forest, chatting idly, the night sound very clear and serene, and everyone savoring it. Suddenly, a song came from the forest:

O maiden, you are the queen of women,

Your bright and kind eyes,

Like the stars in the June night sky,

Shine brilliantly,

Illuminating my subtle steps in the forest,

My beautiful deer,

Let me capture you,

Then a girl continued singing:

Brave hunter,

Come closer to my side,

Never leave,

I will nourish you with the pure milk of my heart:

Climb the high mountain,

Where ten thousand trees provide shelter, we will dwell there.

Anyone would be melted by this song, almost suspecting that it was Theocritus and his Loreidathu out for a night tour (Note 3), but everyone knew that it was Sabuqi and Li Sha singing in harmony.

Time passed, and they continued to love each other passionately.

One day, Sabuqi was crossing the river in the evening, and Li Sha was already standing on the cliff waiting. The weather that day was very bad, with dark clouds and a relentless wind blowing, the waves in the river rolled high like mountains, and there was heavy rain. Li Sha, standing on the cliff, was soaked through, but she didn't move an inch. Her flock of sheep was driven by the heavy rain, and they all scattered and ran into the forest. She seemed to see Sabuqi's small canoe breaking through the waves on the hazy river surface. The sky gradually darkened, and he still hadn't come over. Li Sha continued to watch foolishly. Eventually, her brother came and pulled her back. All night, Li Sha tossed and turned on her pillow, unable to sleep, faintly hearing Sabuqi's cries sadly echoing in the wind and rain.

The night passed, and the sun cheerfully revealed its face as before. A broken canoe drifted on the riverbank. People recognized it as Sabuqi's, and his hunting rifle was still lying in the canoe.

Li Sha went mad from then on. Every day, she would stand on the cliff where she used to wait for Sabuqi to come over, crying. If it was a windy and rainy day, her wails were truly miserable, and anyone who heard them would shed tears.

(Note 1) The male god of love in ancient Oroqen mythology, used here as a lover.

(Note 2) Ayi, a benevolent god in Shamanism.

(Note 3) Two gods, male and female, who were good at singing. Legend has it that they often came out to sing late at night.

Small Bridge 235

— Liu Gongdao

Every time I walk past that newly built Western-style house, I miss the wooden bridge that was torn down.

The original site of that house was a small stream. Because the riverbed was too high, the water only flowed slowly from the gaps in the rocks when the tide rose in the outer river. I would stand on the wooden bridge and watch it twist and turn like a swimming dragon, all the way past the bridge foot and under the wooden posts of a house, to a place I couldn't see. When the tide receded, it would flow back from under the wooden posts, along the original path to the outer river. However, it became so swift and angry, rushing against the rocks that obstructed its path, making a clanging roar like a charging cavalry.

Every day, I stood on the bridgehead, silently facing it as if meeting a lover. I had a dream, a dream of a young girl: she died in this stream.

The young girl had a pair of charming dark eyes, and she also appeared at the bridgehead every day to wash clothes by the river. When I saw her, her black braid was already tied with white yarn. Yes, a lonely child, she desperately needed a man who understood romance to love her, but the man she was in love with had a cowardly heart, and he dared not look directly into her charming dark eyes. She felt disappointed. On a gentle spring evening, like the stream at low tide, she rushed breathlessly into the man's arms in the dark night.

The man bore her a daughter, a girl who couldn't be seen, so she was taken away by the stream, because the man had no way to deal with her…

I still stood on the wooden bridge every day…

The water flowed back and forth every day, damaging the wooden posts of that house. They bought the small river, demolished the bridge, filled the riverbed, and a new Western-style house was built adjacent to the old house.

…So I lost the place I lingered every day!

The mistress of the Western-style house understands music. She plays the piano every day, her music plaintive and weeping, probably because she doesn't know that a romantic young girl is buried under the house?

Every time I walk past her door, I miss the wooden bridge that was torn down.

I want to chase my dream…

Repair 236

— Written by Ma Mengchen

Thunderstorm

Due to the enthusiastic demands of various sectors, we have to rebroadcast "Thunderstorm".

"Thunderstorm" exposes the sordid inside story of an ordinary large family, and Zhou Mansion in the play is a very accurate example.

Zhou Puyuan's second wife is intimate with his son, Zhou Ping, from his first wife, and then Zhou Ping falls in love with Si Feng, the daughter of the servant Lu Gui. However, the second wife's biological son, Zhou Chong, also falls in love with Si Feng.

Lu Gui is a clever man. He knows the secret between his wife, Fan Yi, and the eldest young master, Zhou Ping, and he also knows the secret actions of his own daughter and the eldest young master. This gives him a way to blackmail them and make money.

Movie

The Life Story of Sai Jinhua 243

Who doesn't know Sai Jinhua, who is famous throughout the world? She is the wife of Hong Wenqing, the envoy to the four countries of Russia, Germany, the Netherlands, and Austria. When Hong Wenqing was an envoy, she followed him around the world. In Germany, she was honorably summoned to the palace by Empress Feili every other day to talk. Of course, it goes without saying that at international banquets, she was the most popular and often surrounded by young officers.

Later, Hong Qianchai returned to China, and died a few years later. Sai Jinhua's fate began to show a bleak future day by day.

Sai Jinhua, the widow, had not been there for two months when Mrs. Hong asked two senior officials to talk to her and asked her if she was willing to remain a widow. Sai Jinhua was a very straightforward person, and she honestly asked Mrs. Hong to let her go. The reason was that she was born with a temperament that loved to be lively. Hong Wenqing was dead, and no one was controlling her. She couldn't keep it herself. If she insisted on keeping it, she was afraid that there would be bad rumors. It would really be sorry for Hong Wenzhuan. She wouldn't pretend to deceive people and deceive herself. It was better to leave directly, no matter what happened, it had nothing to do with the Hong family. Moreover, she was only in her twenties at that time, and she was afraid of dying. Why should she defend herself? Where can I keep it!

At that time, three conditions were agreed upon: first, she was not allowed to go to the capital in the short term, as there were too many acquaintances there; second, she was not allowed to flaunt the names of Fu Caiyun and Meng Dai in the future; third, except for the 50,000 yuan in the will and the jewelry and clothes, she was not allowed to demand anything from the Hong family. Under these three conditions, she left the Hong family.

However, she did not receive a penny of the 50,000 yuan in Hong Jiawenqing's will, and it was all swallowed by a young nephew of the Hong family. Later, her life gradually became difficult.

Six years later, in Jiangnan and Pingjin, people were spreading the word about Sai Jinhua, a beautiful woman. This was because she changed her original name to Sai Jinhua in order to fulfill the treaty.

Once, the old lady of Li Shan, the Minister of Household Affairs and concurrently the Deputy of Beiyang Military Affairs, had a birthday. Sai Jinhua rushed to Tianjin to join in the fun. In that carnival of the Li Mansion, Sai Jinhua and Shi Yufang, a servant, became sworn brothers and called each other brothers. And she moved the team from Tianjin to Beijing. This was the time when the Yihe Fist was causing a stir in Tianjin and Beijing. (To be continued)
